Free Talk

Women's Occupations in Europe

— Ren Lun

丨Written Before Chinese Women's Occupations丨

Women's occupations are extremely common in Europe. From company managers to newspaper vendors and postal workers, women have a hand in everything. The doormen of public residences in Paris are mostly women. The positions that men have always held have been half taken away by women in Europe. The reasons for this are: first, there are more women than men in Europe, so women inevitably have to become self-reliant as a result of numerical necessity; second, the rising cost of living in Europe and the increasing vanity of women mean that, on the one hand, men avoid marriage and, on the other hand, the number of women who cannot marry increases daily.

Under the motto of "earn it yourself and spend it yourself!", they mostly spend their wages as they please. Especially with the prevalence of individualism among parents, siblings, and children, it is practically unheard of for children to hand over their earnings to their parents and then ask them for pocket money, as is common in China. As for their spending habits, the first is decoration, being bound by vanity, disregarding their status, and striving to make their clothes increasingly fashionable. Especially young women of considerable age and unsettled blood, intoxicated by freedom and unable to distinguish between good and evil, are constantly susceptible to temptation, and they are precisely decorating themselves with the intention of being tempted. Every holiday, they frequent theaters and dance halls, and their small income is simply not enough.

The Huier Street employment center in Berlin, i.e., what we call a department store, employs thousands of such female clerks. Their ugliness is even more unseen in the Far East. It is said that 80 percent of them suffer from venereal diseases. According to a German newspaper report, a baby born out of wedlock was found in a department store. An investigation revealed that it had been abandoned by a female clerk. As a result, the store conducted a full medical examination of all its employees. Shockingly, out of a thousand female clerks, only two were completely healthy. All the rest were infected with venereal diseases, and the only two healthy ones were young girls aged fifteen and twelve.

Such incidents are not limited to the Huier Street employment center in Germany. Other bank clerks and female ticket sellers at post offices in European countries all have this kind of atmosphere. Even England and Ireland, where the atmosphere is more upright, are not exempt. There is only a difference in quality, not quantity. Seeing this, we in China, where women's occupations are still in their infancy, must be aware of what to pay attention to in our enthusiastic promotion.

Menstruation Does Not Hinder Women's Occupations

— Zhang Zhufeng

丨We Must No Longer Hold This Old European Idea丨

Those who oppose women competing with men for jobs invariably say that women have a unique physiological and intellectual defect not found in men, namely menstruation. This view is not only held by the Chinese, but also by conservatives in the West, such as F. Harrison, who said: "Even if we recognize that men and women are equal in all abilities, menstruation clearly shows the difference in the ability of the two sexes to work." In 1909, the Russian Vozgovsky publicly stated the results of his experiments.

Ms. Wang Hanlun applying her beauty skills.

Ms. Hanlun is a famous movie star who, after leaving the film industry, specialized in beauty skills in Paris. After returning to China, she founded the "Hanlun Beauty Salon" on Avenue Joffre, pioneering women's occupations. (Shen Bao Photographic Society)

, saying that menstruation does have an impact on certain psychology. In fact, he is not credible, because his experiments involved only six women, and all six knew their purpose, so they could not reveal their true feelings. Moreover, the detailed process of his experiments was not described, so we cannot immediately recognize that his conclusions are correct.

In 1914, Dr. AE Arnold published his detailed study of the relationship between his female disciples and menstruation in the January issue of the American Sports Magazine. Based on his experience as a doctor and teacher, he believes that there is no reliable scientific reason for female students not to attend class because of menstruation. At the same time, another female doctor, HollingWorth, conducted long-term and detailed experiments on the issue of women's menstruation, focusing on the speed of intellectual and volitional movements, as well as stability and fatigue, etc. The results proved by the 23 people tested that menstruation does not hinder the development of women's intelligence. Based on this, we cannot use menstruation as a weakness of women and strongly argue that women are therefore not qualified to engage in specialized occupations.

But in reality, there are still many knowledgeable women who are limited by old ideas and the long-standing social discrimination, and they inevitably feel discouraged psychologically and are willing to yield to men; which is a pity. Examining the current social causes of the underdevelopment of women's occupations, although there are many reasons, the deep-rooted old ideas and the unwavering belief of the intellectuals in the women's world; this is truly an attitude of self-closure and ignorance. If not, then the new women should remove this old psychology as soon as possible.

Consider those who argue that women need to give way to men because of menstruation, why don't they allow the female workers they employ to rest temporarily when menstruation comes? Nurses in hospitals are not allowed to rest temporarily because of menstruation; think about it, isn't it worth exposing?

Note: This article is mostly based on the aforementioned thesis of female doctor HollingWorth, excerpted and translated with intent. Readers of her article cannot but feel her spirit of actively promoting women's occupations; I am ashamed that I cannot reach even one-tenth of her level.

The Two Obstacles to Women's Occupations

— Rui Yucheng

丨One is after marriage, and the other is after having children丨

In Chinese society, where customs have long favored men over women, people generally hold two unfavorable attitudes towards women: one is to treat them as toys for men to vent their desires, as if they were prostitutes; the other is to treat them as laborers who serve in the household, as if they were servants. It is pitiful that women have been living under such humiliation for thousands of years, and it is only now that they can finally hold their heads high. People are singing the song of equality between men and women, trying their best to break down the barriers between the two sexes and absolutely make men and women stand on an equal footing. Therefore, women also have the opportunity to serve society. However, under the current social system, women's occupations still cannot escape two obstacles, so that they cannot continue to work hard all the time:

For young girls under the protection of their families, schooling or serving is generally not a problem; because they do not bear any family responsibilities at all, so they are called "open their mouths to eat and stretch their legs to sleep." Wealthy families, of course, have servants to serve them, and poor families also have parents to do it for them, and they cannot bear to let their beloved daughters spend a little effort. But once they marry, under the strict control of their in-laws and among jealous sisters-in-law, no matter what, they cannot tolerate your coming home late after leaving early, and completely enjoying material comforts; therefore, women after marriage, unless they are in a small family and their husbands must be extremely understanding, can have no obstacles to their occupations; otherwise, they can only quit their jobs and take care of the family as housewives. Even if they break through the first obstacle, they may not be able to overcome the second obstacle once they have children! The care of a wet nurse is never as good as taking care of the child yourself. Unless you sew a pocket and carry the child on your back and go out and return with the mother, how can this be done? Therefore, I believe that if women's occupations are to be smooth and unimpeded, we must design to remove these two obstacles!

Please turn to the back page

The Boat Girls of South Lake

— Rong Yu

丨Healthy Beauty Surpasses Modern Women丨

When you arrive at the Jiaxing train station and act like a leisurely tourist, you will be surrounded by many people of the opposite sex. "Want a boat? Going to Misty Rain Tower?" they call out charmingly. Among them are elderly grandmothers, young women, and beautiful young girls. In terms of their profession, we don't distinguish between young and old, and simply call them all "boat girls."

Speaking of the boat girls' attire, they are laborers, so of course they can't compare with the fashionable clothes of young ladies, but they are neatly and cleanly dressed. Their skin color, exposed to the wind and sun, certainly can't be described as fair and tender, but their round arms, thick calves, and brown skin tone perfectly match the current popular idea of "healthy beauty."

Their profession is to row a small boat, ferrying visitors to Misty Rain Tower. Their daily income is uncertain. On good days, especially in hot weather, a round trip can earn a dollar, totaling three or four dollars. On slow days, they might have to go for thirty or forty cents, which is very pitiful.

South Lake is a very round and complete lake, like a pane of glass. Unfortunately, it lacks green mountains on all sides, which is nature's way of not fully completing it. Otherwise, it would compete with West Lake. In the center of the lake is Misty Rain Tower, with its layered buildings and pavilions, shrouded in weeping willows. The scenery is quite lovely. In hot weather, it is even more pleasant to take a fan boat to the tower to cool off. Therefore, the boat girls rely on this lake, this tower, especially during the long, hot summer, to earn a good income.

"An old pearl is worthless." The boat girls, being laborers, must also have this sentiment. Elderly women and young wives don't earn much money per trip. However, young and fashionable girls are different, which leads to many evils. Some frivolous young men use the guise of touring the lake by boat to flirt and seduce. As the saying goes, "The drunkard's intention is not in the wine," this applies to these people. As for the boat girls, without much effort, they are happy to earn more money, without considering that they are disgracing the laboring class. This "pest of women's occupations" should be restrained and punished by local figures.

Most of the boat girls are local village women, with yellow hair, bare feet, and slightly dark skin. They have a natural charm. South Lake is filled with half a lake of water caltrop. Among the fragrant water caltrop flowers, set against the charming and healthy boat girls, there is a sense of artistry and poetic scenery. "Suitable for viewing from afar, but not for frivolous play" is what I hope for the tourists.

Research on Women's Employment Issues

— Yuan Tui

"Education" is the most urgent work丨

At the beginning of the Republic of China, there were women's revolutionary armies and women's political participation associations, but they were short-lived and could not establish a foundation for women's employment. Currently, female staff members are employed in various departments and ministries and provincial offices, such as clerks and secretaries. Although their abilities and knowledge in handling affairs are not inferior to male staff members, ignorant people outside often call them "red vases," implying that they are only for decoration and do not contribute to practical use.

Furthermore, companies and stores, in order to attract customers, often hire female receptionists and sales clerks. When An Shi intended to, he paid attention to women's employment. As things shifted, they even selected a queen, which was not initially expected. I argue that the issue of women's employment is not about a few women who are struggling with marriage and need the help of a women's department. The total number of women in China is about 200 million. Excluding elderly women and newborn girls, there are approximately 100 million middle-aged women and young girls. Among them, I don't know if there are one or two literate people out of ten thousand. Therefore, in studying women's employment now, we should first popularize education, especially promoting half-day schools for women as the first prerequisite.

I remember when I was in Nanjing, there were seven or eight maids in my house. These seven or eight maids were not bought with money, but were the daughters of male and female servants. They ate free meals and provided some service. This was common in large families, but its nature was charitable. When I was sick at home, I taught them to read and write every day. All the young and old children of the neighbors and the young female servants who were willing to attend were taught. This school had no name, so it was called a half-day elementary school for women in the neighborhood. The textbooks were purchased and sent by me, and four tutors were added. Although the school was nominally half-day, it was actually open from morning to night, with eight classes, because these were servants, and they all had things they needed to do, so each lecture was determined by the number of people. If it can be promoted nationwide, many female teachers are needed. In the past, women were engaged in spinning and weaving, but now that there are machines, women have nothing to do all day long, and some do odd jobs. Chinese women must all be literate, or farm, or work, or open shops, in order to have a way to survive. This so-called issue of employment for the majority of women in the country is not something that a few modern women are studying!

Women's Employment and Treatment

— Zhen

丨Relates to Racial Health丨

Today, excellent female talents appear in various businesses. The possibility of women's employment is undoubtedly no longer a question. However, according to the research results of scientists, the concerns about the physiological defects of women should not be ignored. According to the investigation by Dr. Iting of the production conditions of female workers and higher-class women in Stockholm, Sweden, from 1919 to 1922, it was found that the possibility of pregnancy for female workers was 25% lower than that of women in the upper classes, and the infant mortality rate of female workers was 26% higher than that of women in the upper classes. See Oriental Magazine Reprint 丨丨 The prevalence of this maternal disease, malnutrition, is certainly one of the reasons, but even worse is the long periods of sitting and standing, which can affect the development of women's pelvises. This kind of harm not only affects women themselves, but also affects the race.

This is not a defect of women's employment itself, but a defect of the current social system 丨丨 the poor treatment of working women. Therefore, the only way to avoid this kind of harm is to improve treatment:

㈠ Reduce working hours,

㈡ Increase wages,

㈢ Improve the equipment for female workers,

㈣ There must be adequate rest before and after childbirth.

An ancient saying: "It is better to rely on yourself than to ask others for help." On the one hand, political or social efforts must be made for assistance. On the other hand, women's own unity and efforts are still necessary.

Classification of Japanese Women's Occupations

— Bin

丨Can be divided into four categories: intellectual, technical, and physical丨

Promoting women's rights, implementing gender equality, and advocating women's employment have become popular slogans in this new China of the 20th century! However, now, the general new women, relying on a surge of enthusiasm, run around and call out, advocating women's employment, but in the end, they do not see much effect.

An old friend, Mr. Rong, who studied in Japan, returned to China last year due to national difficulties. Yesterday, I met him by chance, and we talked intimately. Later, Mr. Rong talked about the women's occupations in Tokyo, which are very developed. Now, I will describe them in detail below.

According to Mr. Rong, women's occupations in Tokyo are roughly divided into four types:

㈠ Intellectual: such as primary and secondary school teachers, kindergarten nannies, tutors, female doctors, female shop assistants, clerks, postmen, ticket sellers, female reporters, female detectives, librarians, women guards, etc.;

㈡ Technical: such as typists, midwives, accountants, nurses, beauticians, tailors, telephone operators, graphic designers, hairdressers, telecommunications operators, etc.; ㈢ Intellectual and technical: such as actors, actresses, musicians, painters, pianists, etc.;

㈣ Physical: such as dispatch women (similar to female servants in our country), models, waitresses, hotel waitresses (waitresses are female servants), female workers, etc.

The above four types are just a general overview. Due to space limitations, I have to be brief.

Discussion on Women's Occupations

— Chi Fo

Calling them "vases" or "living billboards" is insulting to women. Is it possible to despise women with occupations? I think women's occupations can be divided into three types: The first type is to be a teacher; the second type is to be a businesswoman; and the third type is to be a female worker. In the past, women had no ability to be independent and relied on men, which was very restrictive. On the men's side, the burden was also very heavy. Therefore, when a daughter was born, they said she was a "money-losing commodity." If women have occupations and can be independent, it will lighten the burden on men and allow themselves to be free. It is a very good method. Moreover, the current marriage problem for women is difficult to solve. Do parents make the decision? As a result, things often go wrong: those who are high are not worthy, and those who are low are unwilling to accept. It is really a difficult thing for parents. If women have occupations, they will naturally have social interactions, and their own marriage problems will be easier to solve. Therefore, the "women's occupation problem" is closely related to the "marriage problem."

To promote women's occupations, we must first promote women's education. Therefore, parents must send their daughters to school to study so that they can find noble occupations in the future. If they have not received sufficient education, where can they find good occupations! Women with occupations must still study domestic affairs and manage household affairs. Under no circumstances can they ignore domestic affairs. At the same time, they must work and study concurrently, and they should improve their intelligence in their spare time, reading and studying work, and the two should advance together. Then, they can find better occupations, and the future is even more promising.

The Decline of Women's Occupations

— Wang Dingjiu

The high tide of the times has created the good fortune for women. Large teams of women, waving bright flags, marched forward, standing on the same level as men. "Women's employment" is a way to survive in the midst of the battle!

The new women after the liberation initially made some achievements. But looking at the current situation, one can't help but sigh. Their future is declining!

The facts tell us that the so-called "women's employment" is still a four-character slogan. Only a few can truly establish a foundation and expand the territory for their own occupations. Otherwise, why do female office workers have the nickname "vase"? Most women still tend to be pampered by money, willing to be playthings of men?

Therefore, the result of "women's employment" is that those with high talents become "officials' wives," and those with lower talents become "waitresses." The sisters all drill towards the decadent road, not towards the road to success. There are no amazing women who go to the northwest, but they all put in effort in front of the dressing table!

Speaking of which, our men should also bear part of the responsibility. They should not be destroyers of "women's employment." They should uphold the spirit of human mutual assistance, eliminate the hedgehog-like thoughts, and abandon the attitude of inaction, so as not to hinder the progress of "women's employment" and achieve a state of coexistence and common prosperity.

The sisters should also recognize the current serious situation. The crisis is imminent. Men must take up arms to defend the country. You should be fully responsible for the rear, and carry out a true "pacifying the interior and resisting foreign aggression." The vigorous development of "women's employment" in various countries was caused by the European War. The once-in-a-lifetime opportunity is now at hand. Work hard!

In Front of the Bomei Company

— Shen Bao Photography Agency

The Bomei Company is located at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Seymour Road. It was founded by staff of the Shanghai Young Women's Christian Association and specializes in manufacturing and selling women's products.

Short News

— Yun

Recently, more than a dozen ladies including Liu Wencai, Ling Qishi, and Liang Peishu, in view of the importance of women's employment, jointly founded a Yuyuan Store at the Yuyuan Road entrance of Jing'an Temple. Not only are all the shareholders women, but also the managers and staff are all women. This promotes the true spirit of women's employment and seeks the development of women's occupations. The store is currently in progress, and the goods sold include women's supplies, children's daily necessities, food and beverages, etc., with domestic products and self-made products as the majority. It should be officially opened in early next month.

Conversations About Women's Occupations

— Ji Ping

(Women's employment has long been recognized as one of the most important issues for modern women. This magazine has specially compiled a special issue to openly discuss it in order to arouse the excitement of the women's community. We decided in advance to openly solicit contributions and solicit opinions from experts. The so-called opinions are focused on practical matters and not on empty talk. Therefore, the owner of Ziluolan An thought of Madam Tan Yasheng, the general manager of Yunshang Company, who is currently the most active in advocating women's employment, Madam Gan Jinrong. After his introduction, Madam Tan was very happy and invited me to visit Yunshang and talk about issues related to women's employment.)

Initially, There Were Three Motivations

Madam Tan said straight to the point, "When I took over Yunshang, there were three motivations that came from my heart. I myself regret very much why I didn't start serving society in my golden age, but now I am initially trying the taste of it? I cannot be a pioneer of women's employment, but a laggard of modern women. Wouldn't that be self-conscious!" She changed her tone and said, "However, ordinary women enter the professional world as soon as they leave school, while I have fulfilled the responsibilities of the family and come to repay my long-held wish. This is the first motivation. In recent years, the decline of China's social economy has become irreversible. Perhaps the biggest reason is the dumping of foreign goods and the outflow of profits. Therefore, promoting domestic goods cannot be delayed. I really want to improve women's clothing, change to domestic materials, and shift the wrong idea of women's worshiping foreign goods. This is the second motivation. Yunshang is the product of the hard work of many gentlemen in the literary and artistic circles. If no one is responsible for it and let it evolve naturally, the result will be disappointing to many people. I decided to revitalize it. This is the third motivation."

Related to Women's Decoration

Here, I also think of women's decoration. Modern women, in terms of clothing and beauty, competing for novelty and beauty, has become a common psychology. Among them, I have discovered several interesting facts: There is a kind of Europeanized woman. The clothing or cosmetics she needs in her mind must be bought from foreign countries to be satisfactory. For example, for robe materials, she will not buy domestic georgette, but she must buy foreign lace; for domestic furs, such as fox gray backs, she will not buy them, but she must buy foreign silk, and so on. The psychology of worshiping foreign goods is really inexplicable. There is a kind of women's clothing that is too irrational. They want to be fashionable and decorate well, but they have never paid attention to what kind of clothes are suitable for what occasions? In what season should you wear what kind of clothes? What I said above is the so-called irrational meaning? Unless you are wearing ordinary clothes, it doesn't matter, otherwise there are certain formats for morning, forenoon, afternoon, and evening. For example, modern young ladies or wives wear evening dresses during the day, plus a gray-backed fur coat and gold leather shoes. It is not surprising to go to a grand banquet or dance hall in such dazzling fashion. If you run to Wang Baohe Restaurant or Wufangzhai Noodle Restaurant, wouldn't it be ridiculous? So I think women's clothing, if you don't pay attention to it, it's fine. If you pay attention to it, it must be rational, especially in public places, it is even more important.

Prospects for Women's Employment

I have always been very interested in women's occupations, because I missed the opportunity before, so I admire women with occupations and have great hope for them. Now I will analyze three types of women: ㈠ Married women; ㈡ Women who are currently in the professional world; ㈢ Girls who are preparing for employment in their study days. What I hope for them is that married women have very important responsibilities for handling domestic affairs, the kindness of their husbands, and the upbringing of their children. Being good at managing the family and being a good wife and mother has fulfilled the duties of a woman. Even if she does not work in the professional world, her contribution to society and the country is already very significant, so there is no need to be confined to serving outside; women who are already in the professional world should strengthen their will, respect their own status and reputation, not be tempted by money, and not be fascinated by emotions, to break the encirclement of the current bad environment and open up a bright road; girls in school days should first consider their own ambitions and circumstances and prepare early. When they have sufficient knowledge and have learned the methods of dealing with people, things, and the world, there will be no difficulties in being incompatible with society.

Commonly Seen Malpractices

Most female comrades in the professional world can strive to be upward, but at the same time, several malpractices have been discovered, such as: ㈠ Being fond of novelty and fashion, over-decorating, giving people the nickname of red vase; ㈡ Having less sense of responsibility for their duties; ㈢ For the sake of vanity, they often change their minds and have no perseverance; ㈣ Going out to serve and abandoning the natural duties of the family. Let me give an example: A certain lady is very talented. Since taking office as the secretary of a certain provincial government, she must travel by car and is very generous. The monthly salary is not enough to support herself. She entrusts her children at home to maids and does not take care of them at all. A'nan cries hungry and cold all day long, and A'da and A'er either quarrel with the children next door or break their foreheads and scalps. Such a gain does not outweigh the loss. Misunderstanding the true meaning of women's employment, no one will agree with it, right?

Madam Tan talked very enthusiastically, but unfortunately it was too early, so I ended the interview.

Li Guojie Placed Under Surveillance Yesterday

Zhu Jia骅 Convened a Meeting of New Directors and Supervisors Yesterday

Discussing the Bureau's Mortgage at the Municipal Government

New Staff to Take Over This Morning

According to a Central News Agency reporter's investigation, the matter of the China Merchants Bureau mortgaging to the American China Trading Company for a loan of ten million taels, using the Zhongbei and Huasan wharves as collateral, is confirmed. The signing of the mortgage contract by Li Guojie, the general manager of the Bureau, was approved and filed on September 3rd under the instruction of the Supervision Department of the China Merchants Bureau under the Ministry of Communications, and was approved in advance by the former Minister of Communications, Chen Mingshu. In addition to the signature of Li Guojie, the general manager of the China Merchants Bureau, the mortgage contract was also stamped by the supervisor, Chen Fumu. It is also heard that Minister of Communications Zhu Jia骅 and Director of Navigation Affairs Gao Tingzi went to Shanghai to understand the mortgage situation. At 3:00 PM yesterday, they convened a discussion meeting at the Municipal Government with the new general manager of the Bureau, Liu Hongsheng, and others. Li Guojie was also present. After Li Guojie reported the details of the mortgage, he admitted the errors in the procedures and reported himself. The Municipal Government, under orders, placed Li Guojie under temporary surveillance pending investigation. The new general manager, Liu Hongsheng, is scheduled to take over this morning after the establishment of the Bureau's Board of Directors and Supervisors. The details are recorded as follows:

Therefore, he mortgaged to the American China Trading Company for a loan of ten million taels (not ten million yuan), using the Zhongbei and Huasan wharves as collateral. The debts of the China Merchants Bureau are accumulated, and the ships and warehouses are dilapidated, resulting in a monthly income of more than 100,000 yuan, which is not enough to cover expenses. If thorough improvements are not made as soon as possible, bankruptcy will inevitably occur. According to the report, we have contacted the American China Trading Company, the Dalae Shipping Company, and others regarding the construction loans in the Bund and Fuzhou Road areas of Shanghai, the mortgage of the Shanghai Zhongbei and Huaxin Nanwu wharves, the lease agreement of the Shanghai Zhongbei and Huasan wharves, and the memorandum of understanding on purchasing ships on credit. After repeated consultations by the former Commissioner Guo Waifeng and the General Manager, and after review by this department, the articles of the contract are feasible and should be approved and filed in accordance with the regulations. The General Manager is instructed to sign the above-mentioned contracts with the American merchants, etc., and the borrowed funds should be used entirely for the purpose of clearing outstanding debts. All the remaining funds should be designated for construction and production, so as to turn the tide of the stagnant situation and avoid the loan being wasted and increasing debts. You must comply with this order. The attached documents are stored concurrently. Supervisor Chen Fumu."

Song Ziwen Flew to Hangzhou Yesterday

Delivered an Important Speech Before Departure

Describing the Reasons for the Reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau

Developing the Shipping Industry to Benefit Industry and Commerce

Song Ziwen, Acting President of the Executive Yuan, flew from Hankou to Hangzhou the day before yesterday to inspect the aviation school and returned to Shanghai in the afternoon. Yesterday, Song delivered a speech on the reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau and invited Liu Hongsheng, Shi Liangcai, Ye Zuotang, and others to his residence at 3:30 PM to discuss matters related to the China Merchants Bureau. At 4:20 PM, Song, accompanied by his secretary Huang Chundao, took a plane to Hangzhou. The details are as follows:

▲ Song Delivers Speech: Song said in his speech yesterday: "The shipping industry is closely related to national transportation, agriculture, industry, and commerce. Among the shipping companies in China, the China Merchants Bureau was established the earliest and has the largest scale. The government has maintained it through various means, but internal conflicts often arise among the shareholders, and the administrators are incapable, leading to numerous malpractices and increasing corruption. Looking at the foreign shipping companies established at the same time as the China Merchants Bureau, they have all expanded more than tenfold, but the China Merchants Bureau has only regressed and not progressed. The ships are outdated, most of them are more than 30 years old, and many have sunk over the years. Not only is the company's loss immeasurable, but the safety of passengers and goods is also worrying, and the shipping industry is declining day by day, and shipping rights are deteriorating day by day, which is a fundamental concern for the country and society. Since the establishment of the National Government, supervisors have been repeatedly dispatched to supervise and reorganize the situation, but the situation is too complicated and difficult to reorganize. The development of national agriculture, industry, and commerce is advancing in tandem with the shipping industry. If the shipping industry cannot be reorganized, the agriculture, industry, and commerce will be affected. The China Merchants Bureau was established the earliest, and the location occupied by the wharf is superior to any company. However, for various reasons, it cannot fulfill its function to serve the society. At the same time, dividends have not been paid for more than ten years. In the past three years, the market price of stocks has averaged only thirty taels per set. In view of the importance of the shipping industry and for the sake of the shareholders, the government has decided to nationalize the China Merchants Bureau, and all stocks are set at fifty taels in cash per set, which has been submitted to the Central Political Council for resolution and approval. The government is willing to pay this relatively high price at a time of financial difficulty, hoping to create a modern shipping company on the existing foundation to promote the development of agriculture, industry, and commerce. The shareholders have not received interest for more than ten years, and the government's offer to recover at a price exceeding the market price by twenty taels shows the government's preferential intention, and most are happy to accept it. At the same time, although the government has taken over the nationalization, it still appoints people with prestigious reputation from all walks of life to take charge of the matter. In view of the past history of the China Merchants Bureau and the current situation of various countries, the government's management of the shipping industry by ordinary officials will be ineffective. Secondly, the concentration of forces from all walks of life can make the shipping industry easier to reorganize. Thirdly, this time is entirely for the purpose of developing the social economy and agriculture, industry, and commerce, so the directors and supervisors appointed are absolutely unrelated to politics. After that, the political situation may change, but the foundation of the China Merchants Bureau will not be shaken by it. The China Merchants Bureau has accumulated huge losses, and this year has already lost more than 1.7 million. The government's nationalization at this time has no benefits to speak of. One is that the global economic situation is not good, the second is that the reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau takes time, and the third is that the government's purpose is to promote the development of the shipping industry to benefit agriculture, industry, and commerce. After the takeover, the loss-making routes must also be carried out, from domestic routes to foreign routes, even at the cost of sacrifice. Since the government is frankly seeking benefits for the people, it hopes that all sectors of society will unite and work together, and everyone will regard the reorganization and development of the China Merchants Bureau as an important responsibility, so that the progress of China's shipping industry can be expected."

▲ Flight to Hangzhou: At 3:30 PM yesterday, Song invited Liu Hongsheng, General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau, Shi Liangcai, Standing Director, Ye Zuotang, Du Yuesheng, Yang Ying, Directors Qian Xinzhi, Hu Yunzhuang, Hu Bijiang, Wang Xiaolai, Supervisors Yu Qiaqing, Qin Runqing, Lu Xuepu, and others to Song's residence on Qiqi Road to discuss the problem of the China Merchants Bureau. The meeting lasted about half an hour before it was dismissed. Song then took a car to Hongqiao Airport and boarded a Sikorsky plane at 4:10 PM and flew to Hangzhou. Duan, the consultant of Zhang Xueliang, is still staying in Hankou and did not come to Shanghai with Song this time.

Annual General Meeting of the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Economic Society

Chen Guangfu and Li Fusun Give Important Speeches

The Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Economic Society held its 4th First Annual General Meeting and Academic Lecture at the Banking Club yesterday. Dai Ailu, Jin Guobao, Chen Guangfu, Cai Zhengya, Chen Qilu, Ye Yuan, Li Fusun, Li Zhaohuan, Pan Xulun, Xu Xinliu, Wang Zhixin, He Dekui, Xu Yongzuo, Li Fuhou, Zhuang Zhihuan, and others totaling thirty-six people and seven or eight guests were in attendance. At noon, they were seated for lunch, after which the meeting was opened. Chairman Dai Ailu reported that Zhang Gongquan and Chen Guangfu were originally invited to give speeches, but Mr. Zhang had to return to his hometown due to business. Mr. Li Fusun had just returned from Nanyang, so he was invited to give a lecture. Afterwards, Chen Guangfu and Li Fusun gave speeches in succession. Dai Ailu, He Dekui, and others made inquiries, and then discussed the affairs of the society before adjourning. The details are recorded below.

Chen Guangfu's Speech: Mr. Chen's topic was "A Way to Solve China's Economic Problems." He briefly stated that he had recently toured and investigated the Yangtze River and the North for four months, traveling from Nanjing, Wuhu, Jiujiang, Hankou, to Zhengzhou, Kaifeng, Beijing, Tianjin, Jinan, and Qingdao, and then returned to Shanghai. He felt that the Yangtze River Basin was the richest area in China, but after the great flood, it was full of scars and could not be restored in a short period of time. The situation in Henan was better than the previous year, as it had not suffered from war and the people were able to live a minimum of security. The facilities of the cultural institutions in Kaifeng were more complete than those in Shanghai. Tianjin was affected by the international depression and the numerous taxes and levies in the Zhangjiakou area, resulting in a decrease in the export of wool and other products, which was quite depressed. The situation in Shandong was even better than that in Henan, because the annual output of tobacco leaves, straw hat cords, food, etc. to other places was worth 200 million yuan. The society had a large amount of circulation, so the current situation was very good. He really felt the greatness of the Chinese people's struggle in terms of livelihood. Once the war stops, the recovery will be quite rapid. However, China's economy is very closely related to international relations and is affected by the world everywhere. This topic only refers to the domestic situation, and whether it can be successful is still uncertain. He hoped that everyone would have opinions to teach him. 1. The Reasons for Capital Flowing to Shanghai: Regarding the problem of cash concentration in Shanghai, some people blamed the banks. In fact, the banks were also very willing to release funds to the interior, but this was not within the banks' ability. The reasons were roughly: A. Political instability and insecurity in the interior; B. Credit tightening: In the past, when tea, silk, wheat, and rice were on the market, cash flowed from Shanghai to the interior. Also, due to the sale of cloth, sugar, kerosene, flour, cigarettes, etc. in the interior, cash flowed back to Shanghai. Compared with previous years, the national trade deficit was supplemented by remittances from overseas Chinese, while the interior was supplemented by credit loans. For example, the loans from Shanghai banks to the Zhenyang area and the loans from Ningbo money houses to Hankou exceeded millions each year. In recent years, the floods have caused many bad debts. As a result, not only were they unwilling to continue lending, but they also gradually recovered the loans that had already been released. The position of the bank was to use funds on behalf of depositors, and the psychology of depositors was to flock to the safest option. If they recognized a slight crisis, they would immediately withdraw their funds. The second was the protection of the law. The old laws have been abolished, and the new laws have not yet become a habit. The debtors are not afraid of the law and even regard defaulting on debts as an honor, especially in the interior. 2. The Problems of Shanghai Itself: Among the new businesses in the past twenty years, the progress of banks has been the fastest. In the early stages of the business, foreigners often laughed at its difficulty in succeeding, but now most of the cash in the country has been concentrated in banks operated by Chinese. However, there are still many weaknesses: A. There is no true bank of banks to back it up; B. Too much investment in speculative businesses; C. The stagnation of industrial loans; D. The value of various stocks has no value as securities and cannot be circulated in society, resulting in a decrease in funds. 3. The Difficulties in Relieving the Rural Areas: The main reason is that the farmers lack knowledge, and they become poorer because of their ignorance, and they become more ignorant because of their poverty. It is not easy to start relief and there is a lack of protection. 4. The Prerequisites for Money to Be Securely Transferred to the Interior: The interior must be peaceful, investors must break the mentality of relying on concessions, and the law must be protected. The ways are: A. For the relief of small and medium-sized cities in the interior, the original financial institutions should be used to fully support good money houses and guide them to gradually shift from credit to people to credit to things; B. For the relief of special rural areas, various cooperatives should be used, such as the Shanghai Bank and the Chinese and Foreign Relief Society's cooperatives in North China and the Wujiang Cooperative in Anhui. The results of lending cooperatives are excellent; C. For the relief of old-fashioned rural areas, the original financial institutions, such as pawnshops, should also be used. The knowledgeable people in the pawnshops in various places should find ways to improve them, reduce interest rates, and cooperate with the financial industry. In terms of business, they should not rush to wear and tear clothes, but should extend to commodities such as rice and wheat, so as to gradually establish cooperatives, etc.

Li Fusun's Speech: Mr. Li's topic was "Observations from a Visit to Nanyang." He briefly stated that he had been in Nanyang for fourteen days, and because the communication was simple and the visits and inspections were arranged in advance, he was able to gain something even though the time was short. Overseas Chinese in Nanyang accounted for six-tenths of the total residents, and almost all commercial and economic power was in the hands of the overseas Chinese. However, in recent years, the price of pepper, rubber, and tin ore has plummeted, resulting in many losses. Most of the overseas Chinese who went to Nanyang in the past did not have concrete plans and long-term vision. At that time, pepper, rubber, and tin ore were very profitable, so some people borrowed money to invest, but they gradually plummeted, and most of them went bankrupt. However, those who operated with their own capital were able to survive with difficulty. Although some of them had thick assets, they had very narrow-minded prejudices and no ambition to cooperate. Most of the overseas Chinese students had no concept of the motherland, but there were also many overseas Chinese compatriots and some overseas Chinese students who loved the country. They remitted 300 million yuan to the motherland every year, but they also felt very painful in their lives, and their businesses were gradually declining. If there was no relief, they would fail completely. Many businesses have been transferred to foreign hands, such as the shipping companies that travel between Nanyang, Shantou, and Xiamen, etc., and a certain company has also been mortgaged to foreign banking groups. However, with the slight increase in the value of rubber, there is still hope for business development to be recovered. The most important thing recently is the merger of the Hua Feng, Overseas Chinese, and Hua Shang banks. In the past, the three banks competed fiercely, and after the lending was contracted, they competed with each other in remittance, resulting in losses for each. The last time Mr. Zhang Gongquan traveled to Nanyang and persuaded them to merge, and after several negotiations, it was finally settled, and the name was set as Overseas Chinese Bank, with a capital of 10 million Singapore dollars, with 40 yuan per share. However, the investment scope was narrow and the capital was lacking, resulting in a market price of only 20 yuan per share. He suggested that a domestic banking group buy a part of the shares to increase capital and avoid being bought by foreign merchants, which is still under consideration. He hoped that Chinese people would export more domestic goods and purchase goods produced and operated by overseas Chinese and invest in established businesses to save the crisis faced by overseas Chinese.

▲ Shanghai Branch Meeting: After the lectures, the affairs of the society were discussed and resolved as follows: 1. Amend Article 9 of the branch's regulations, such as: "In addition to paying the society's fees, members of the branch shall pay 2 yuan per year, and friends of the society shall pay 1 yuan per year." 2. Hold a symposium every month. The topic of discussion next month will be the problem of rural economy. Those who have opinions and wish to join the discussion should notify the branch secretary, Mr. Wang Zhixin. 3. Cai Zhengya reported on the work of the Sino-Japanese Trade Research Association. The statistical work of Sino-Japanese trade has been mostly completed, and the research part of Sino-Japanese trade has been less than Beijing's. It was decided to raise more funds to continue the work.

Representatives of Overseas Chinese Merchants from Vietnam Petitioning Return to Shanghai

Discussing the Petitioning Process

Representatives Offering Opinions

Scheduled to Return to Vietnam by Ship

Due to the Sino-French Vietnam Treaty, which China had already announced but the French government had not yet ratified, goods from China have been cut off, threatening the economic ruin of hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese in Vietnam. The Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Southern Vietnam decided to send Mr. Huang An and Mr. Xu Yixian back to China to petition the government and negotiate with the French. Last week, they arrived in Beijing from Shanghai, stayed for a week, and petitioned the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. Yesterday, they returned to Shanghai. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency interviewed Mr. Huang and Mr. Xu yesterday at their residence, and they discussed the details of their trip to Beijing to petition.

▲ Petitioning Process

Mr. Xu stated that they arrived in Beijing last Monday and immediately submitted their petitions to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. They were graciously received by Minister Luo, Vice Minister Xu, and Commissioners Zhou Qigang, Chen Shuren, and Xiao Jishan of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. The representatives explained the suffering of the overseas Chinese, and Minister Luo offered comforting words, saying that the French envoy to China was scheduled to arrive in Beijing on Tuesday and that he would do his best to negotiate with him at that time. Commissioner Zhou and others moved the representatives to the Overseas Chinese Reception Center for accommodation and treated them with great courtesy. On Tuesday, the French envoy arrived in Beijing, and due to foreign custom, negotiations could not begin immediately, but a banquet was held. The next day (Wednesday), they met with Vice Minister Xu Mo, who informed them that the French envoy had telegraphed the French government for instructions regarding the Vietnam treaty, and the future looked promising, as the French envoy's attitude was very positive. The representatives, mindful that the French government had not yet ratified the Vietnam treaty and that the sticking point was the list of goods, requested Vice Minister Xu to hand over the annex to the treaty (i.e., the list of goods) for study, which was granted. The representatives then conducted a lengthy study and found some areas that were not entirely satisfactory.

▲ Offering Opinions

The annex to the treaty was divided into two parts, one for China and one for France, listing the most-favored-nation tariff items requested for import by each country. China had twenty-three items listed, while France had only six. Upon closer inspection, the items listed by China, with the exception of a few, such as leather, which were popular in Vietnam, were generally irrelevant to the goods used by overseas Chinese. The six items listed by France were all fast-selling products in China, while the twenty-three items requested by China were actually not applicable to the overseas Chinese in Vietnam. The representatives then requested Vice Minister Xu to introduce them to Zhang Weihan, Secretary-General of the Legislative Yuan, who was familiar with the treaty, to discuss adding silk, tea, porcelain, and Chinese medicinal materials, which were most suitable for the overseas Chinese in Vietnam, to the most-favored-nation tariff list, and also adding the originally specified leather and other items. It was decided that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' European and American Affairs Department would retain the representatives' proposal, who solemnly declared that the principle for future negotiations with the French would be based on the newly revised list of goods. Vice Minister Xu expressed his agreement. The representatives believed that the purpose of their petition had been fulfilled, and they left Beijing to return to Shanghai.

▲ Consular Visas

Regarding the issue of consular visas, the arrangements for this matter in Vietnam have been properly handled. After the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a notice, the matter had already been implemented in areas where consulates were stationed. Because the treaty with Vietnam had not yet been finalized and consulates had not been established, the issue of visas could not be discussed. This time, when the two representatives, Huang and Xu, went to Beijing, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs entrusted the chairman of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Southern Vietnam with the task of handling cargo visas to facilitate commerce.

▲ Scheduled to Return to Vietnam

It has been two weeks since the representatives Huang and Xu returned to China. Now that everything has been settled, they are scheduled to return to Vietnam on the French mail ship General Metzinger on the 19th of this month. It is reported that the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Association will hold a meeting before the representatives leave Shanghai to discuss assistance to the overseas Chinese and to welcome Mr. Huang and Mr. Xu.

The donation notice is recorded below to inspire schools and institutions in various places to launch their own initiatives, as follows: Donation Notice for the Northeast Volunteer Army: The Northeast Volunteer Army is fighting against the violent Japanese with flesh and blood, and they are now facing a harsh winter with meager clothing and supplies. Various circles have separately initiated the collection of donations. All colleagues at the university have long harbored righteous indignation and will surely be happy to support this cause. A standard has been tentatively drafted, with each person donating one percent of their monthly salary for six months, advanced by the university to meet the urgent needs, which will then be deducted from each person's salary in monthly installments, starting from October and ending in March of next year. I have always been fond of studying traditional Chinese medicine and am a member of medical organizations and have a license to practice medicine issued by the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau. My intention has always been to care for the suffering of my compatriots, but I have other occupations and little free time. The world is chaotic, and I have no time to spare. Therefore, my medical practice is limited to family members and close friends, and I do not wish to publicize it to outsiders. This is known to those who have had a brief encounter with Juecai. Today, upon seeing this news, I could not help but feel a compassion I have never felt before. Although I do not have the means to donate a large sum of money to aid the volunteer army, I know that a generous donor has a difficult-to-treat disease, and if I remain silent and do not offer help, my conscience would not allow it. Juecai's mailing address is: Translation Department, Shanghai Railway Bureau, No. 257 Old Bazi Road. Also, Juecai has suffered from insomnia in the past, and my wife also suffers from it now. Both of us have been cured using traditional Chinese medicine and have never had a single injection. Juecai's writing of this letter is purely out of a sense of conscience, and all obligations have been fulfilled first. I hope you will take this into consideration. This is a respectful greeting to you, Wang Juecai, written on November 16th.

Received Warning Letters a Month Ago

Yongchang Silk, Satin, Wool, and Cotton Cloth Shop, owned by Jin Zouting of Suzhou, located at No. 64 Zhengjia Muqiao Street in the French Concession, was suddenly attacked by two men in their twenties, wearing Chinese-style clothing, who were loitering in front of the shop at 5:20 PM yesterday. County Land Survey Fee Verified and Collected

Cancellation of Rounding Up Original Proposal

The Shanghai County Government and the Finance Bureau jointly issued an announcement yesterday stating: It has been ordered by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance and Department of Civil Affairs: Regarding the collection of land survey fees in various counties, the fee of one jiao per mu will be collected, and those who have less than one mu will be charged as if they had one mu, and receipts will be issued separately. This was implemented in Jiangning and Zhenjiang Counties in the 18th year of the Republic of China when the land survey fee was first collected, and the method was decided by the former Land Consolidation Committee and drafted by the Provincial Department of Finance and issued separately for compliance. Now, citizens such as Sheng Yuanyin, Wang Tinggan, and Wu Weihe of Songjiang County have telegraphed to request that the land survey fee be collected based on the existing practice of verifying the amount. After the two provincial departments reviewed the matter and received a reply from the Provincial Land Bureau, they agreed that the method of charging less than one mu as one mu had many drawbacks and should be improved in a timely manner. The request of the citizens was approved, and the original proposal to round up to the nearest mu was canceled. From this year onward, in addition to those already collected, the land survey fee in each county should be verified and collected based on past practices. For example, if the fee is 1 jiao and 1 fen per mu, then the fee for 1 mu and 1 fen should be 1 jiao and 1 fen, and so on, to ensure fairness and prevent abuse. In addition to the order and report to the Provincial Government for filing, the County Magistrate is ordered to comply and instruct the Finance Bureau to comply. At the same time, a joint announcement will be made to inform all. The County Magistrate must submit a report on the implementation to the Provincial Departments. Therefore, it is hereby announced that the land survey fees in this county have been discussed and resolved at the 119th County Government Meeting to be collected from this year onward. In addition to the fact that the fees for the second phase of the land price tax will be verified and calculated, it is hereby announced to inform all residents of the county.

Fuyang County Suffers Banditry, Begs for Relief

Yu Bandit Li Chenggong and Others Run Rampant

The Anhui Fellow-Provincials Association and the Fuyang County Fellow-Provincials Association recently received telegrams from the county relief branch, various organizations, and legal groups, stating that Fuyang has suffered successive water and drought disasters, and the people are deeply impoverished. Unexpectedly, Yu Bandit Li Chenggong's group and Zhang Si's and Zhao Hongshan's groups, each numbering several thousand, have recently invaded the county, burning, killing, raping, and looting. The villages they pass through are left in ruins. In the tenth district alone, more than fifty villages have been destroyed, and corpses are everywhere. At least 250,000 people are left alive or have escaped after being abducted and have no home to return to. The suffering is unbearable to describe. Now that severe winter is approaching, they are exposed to the wind and sleep in the open, and people are dying every day. Local finances are exhausted, and there is no way to remedy the situation. We hope that various relief organizations, charity groups, and philanthropists will quickly provide clothing and food to provide relief and protect these survivors from filling ditches. The words are almost written in blood and tears. It is reported that the provincial association and the Fuyang County Shanghai Student Association are preparing to request relief from various charity organizations or to raise cotton clothing, food, and cash to be sent directly to the county relief branch for immediate distribution.

Anhui People Unanimously Oppose the Rice Surtax

The Anhui Native Association in Shanghai and the Anhui Students Association in Shanghai Reiterate Their Telegram to Wu Zhongxin Questioning the Disastrous and Oppressive Rice Surtax in Anhui. Respected Mr. Wu Zhongxin of Anqing: Your esteemed telegram has been received. The illegal and oppressive rice surtax has been met with fervent opposition from Anhui people everywhere. Public opinion is clearly against it. Instead of acceding to popular sentiment by removing and punishing Jiang and Ye, you have resolutely dismantled the Grain Administration, only to then expand its organization, establish numerous branch bureaus and inspection stations, setting up a dense network of taxation, exhausting the resources of the people. This is still not enough, as you have decided to issue a massive road construction bond of five million yuan, secured by the rice surtax revenue. The people, already on the verge of death, are being bled dry. How can you bear to exploit them repeatedly? The people of Anhui bear no grudge against you. Why are you so swayed by sycophants, determined to inflict such extreme harm on Anhui? The fellow villagers in Shanghai deeply resent this. Therefore, a joint conference of all sectors was held on the [Eastern] Day, unanimously vowing to fight to the death. In addition to the representatives Liu Zhujing, Ling Shuqiao, Xu Zhiyuan, Dai Gaowu, Fan Zhenbang, Fang Chen, Xu Huanran, and other comrades who left for the province today to petition, we are sending this telegram as a final appeal. We earnestly hope that you will act decisively, abolish the Rice Surtax Bureau and all its personnel, eliminate this institution, and halt the issuance of public bonds. Then, the provincial administration will be renewed, criticism will cease, and public support will be no less than when you first took office. This urgent plea is respectfully submitted for your understanding. The Anhui Native Association in Shanghai and the Anhui Students Association in Shanghai respectfully kowtow. Attached is the Second Notice of the Meeting to Discuss the Rice Surtax: Respected Sirs, This is to inform you that reports have arrived in Shanghai regarding the situation of the delegation petitioning against the rice surtax in various places. All matters relating to this issue urgently need further discussion. It is hereby scheduled that the Second General Meeting of all sectors of Anhui natives in Shanghai to oppose the rice surtax will be held at 2:00 PM on the 13th of this month (i.e., Sunday) at the Native Association in Pu Bai Fang, Rue Luban, to jointly deliberate for further action. The Anhui Native Association in Shanghai and the Anhui Students Association in Shanghai jointly announce.

Furthermore, the Anhui Students Association in Beijing Appeals Against Oppressive Levies and Ruthless Exactions: All citizens inside and outside Anhui province, take note! Dispatches report the Anhui authorities’ rampant levies and ruthless exactions, causing widespread outcry. In addition to sending telegrams to Wu and Ye, demanding the immediate cancellation of all kinds of oppressive levies, this association earnestly solicits unanimous support. This is our hope and prayer. However, the recent establishment of the Grain Administration, the public sale of opium, and the unauthorized issuance of road construction bonds worth five million yuan are harsh policies that harm the people and ruin the country, policies more ferocious than tigers. You are a wise man; we hope you will swiftly retract your orders and not become a continuation of the Chen [Diaoyuan] regime. The Anhui Students Association in Beijing [Gray]. (2) Telegram to Director Ye of the Finance Department: Respected Mr. Ye Yuanlong of the Anhui Finance Department, in recent years, our unfortunate Anhui has suffered repeated disasters, leaving homes devastated and the people impoverished. Yet the provincial authorities have boldly established the Grain Administration, levying a rice surtax, a heavy plunder of six jiao per dan, draining the pond to catch all the fish. How can the people’s lives bear this? Despite clear orders from the Ministry of Finance to abolish it, they brazenly disregard them. The Anhui Students Association in Beijing [Gray].

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Will Expand the Municipal Ferry

Adding One Large Ferry and Three Small Ferries

Opening a New Line from Wusong to the 16th Pier

The Municipal Ferry, run by the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, has not only provided great convenience to the citizens, but the bureau has also created the most complete and modern ferry at the lowest cost, which has been praised by both Chinese and foreigners. The bureau currently has four large ferries and three small ferries, but due to overcrowding, they are not sufficient to meet demand. Therefore, it is now planned to add one large ferry and three small ferries. As soon as this is approved by this week's municipal meeting, work can begin. According to Director Huang of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, speaking to a reporter from the Central News Agency, the three small ferries to be added are for use on cross-river routes. They can travel in both directions because the river surface is narrow, and there are many boats. Turning the ferry around is both troublesome and dangerous. The small ferry that travels in both directions not only eliminates the need to turn around, saving time, but also eliminates danger. The large ferry to be added is for use on the new route from Wusong Town to the 16th Pier. It is very troublesome for merchants in Wusong to go to the 16th Pier to purchase goods. If the new route from Wusong Town to the 16th Pier is opened, it will be much more convenient. In addition, all ferries purchased will use diesel engines, so passengers can avoid the discomfort of coal ash blowing in their faces.

Dollar and American Mail Steamship Companies

Shorten the Sino-American Voyage by One Day

The Zi Lin Bao [North China Daily News] reports that the San Francisco liners of the Dollar Steamship Company and the American Mail Steamship Company will now shorten the voyage by one day, reducing the journey from Shanghai to San Francisco to seventeen days. This will begin with the Grant President liner on the 10th of next month. Thereafter, the departure date of the San Francisco liners from Shanghai will also be changed from Friday to Saturday. Furthermore, the round-the-world liners of the two companies coming to Shanghai from San Francisco can also depart from Shanghai one day earlier, starting with the Sea Zang Shi President liner on the 22nd of this month. Thereafter, the departure date will be changed to Tuesday, heading to Europe for export.

The District Court Strictly Prohibits Flower Gambling

Flower gambling in this port, with its main operation located in the foreign concession, is organized by a group of hooligans including Cao, Gao, and Mao. It operates three times a day, with thousands of listening posts throughout Shanghai, and the number of errand runners dispatched from these listening posts reaches over ten thousand. The means of luring gamblers are so numerous, and the number of victimized, foolish people is staggering. The daily income is beyond calculation. In the Chinese areas of Nanshi, Zhabei, Pudong, and Huxi, the listening posts and errand runners are also countless. Every evening, passersby stand waiting for swift horses to bring news, and the crowds are especially dense along the Road of the Republic. This phenomenon has come to the attention of the Jiangsu High Court. Cases of families being ruined, suicides, and murders caused by flower gambling are frequent, making it a great scourge of society. Therefore, the High Court has instructed the Shanghai District Court to immediately arrest and detain the worst offenders and to make every effort to suppress it in order to uphold the law. Therefore, the District Court instructed the Judicial Police Department to closely and promptly arrest and bring the offenders to justice, and to announce to the public that reports are permitted, so that the ringleaders can be investigated and punished.

Appeal to the Supreme Court in the Russian Beggar Case

In the case of Russian beggar Georgiy Laty Love, who died of illness in the Second Special District District Court detention center on June 19 of this year, his brother, Simon Gray Techy, reported to the French Concession Police Department that the warden of the detention center, Xu Chongwen, the medical officer of the detention center, Yu Ming Gao, and the cell guard, Zhou Zongxiang, were being prosecuted by the Second Special District District Court for abandonment and injury resulting in death. After a trial was held, and the Shanghai-renowned English and French medical officers were invited to re-examine the corpse with the forensic doctor of this court, the result was that he died of illness. Subsequently, the three defendants were found not guilty. The Police Department was dissatisfied with the original judgment and filed an appeal to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. When the trial was concluded, the appeal was dismissed. It has been repeatedly recorded in previous reports that the Police Department was still not convinced by the second-instance judgment and had already filed an appeal with the Supreme Court in Nanjing, the third-instance body. The High Court Third Branch has submitted the files to the higher court for review. The Police Department is now collecting the previous statements of all parties concerned to supplement the written reasons for the appeal.

Japanese Cement Masquerades as National Product "Horse Brand"

Domestic Cement Business Accuses Shen Tai Hang and Others

The Domestic Cement Business Office, located at No. 6 Sichuan Road, has always operated the "Horse Brand" cement, promoting it nationwide. Recently, the office learned that Shen Tai Brick and Tile Shop at No. 9 Weishui Lane, Ningbo Road, and the Meichang Construction Factory at No. 101 Zhili Road, Beijing Road, jointly purchased more than 120 bags of Japanese "Ship Brand" cement, changed the labels to "Horse Brand", and transported them into the factory in the hope of avoiding inspection and obtaining huge profits. Therefore, the lawyer was retained to accuse Jia Jisheng, the owner of Shen Tai Brick and Tile Shop, and his councillor, Wu Wenyue, and Xu Qingxiang, the manager of Meichang Construction Factory, of the crime of hindering agriculture, industry, and commerce. The judge Huang Risheng of the Ninth Criminal Tribunal of the First Special District Court of Shanghai summoned them to court in the afternoon. Wang An, the representative of the Domestic Cement Business Office, testified that the cement operated by his office had three trademarks: "Horse Brand," "Elephant Brand," and "Taishan Brand," with "Horse Brand" being the most well-known nationwide. The defendants colluded on the 12th of last month to purchase more than 120 bags of Japanese "Ship Brand" cement, falsely labeled them with the "Horse Brand" trademark, and transported them from the Huishan Wharf to the Meichang Construction Factory to prevent inspection. His office learned of this and immediately sent someone to report to the Huishan Patrol Station. The patrol station then sent Chinese and Western detectives to the Meichang Construction Factory to investigate and found many bags of cement falsely labeled with the "Horse Brand" trademark. The Chinese and Western detectives took the defendant Wu Wenyue to the patrol station. The patrol station said that this case was a private prosecution, so it allowed Wu Wenyue to be released on bail. Therefore, he specially retained a lawyer to sue the defendants. Subsequently, Hua Tan Wang Xiangpo of the Huishan Patrol Station reported that on the 12th of last month at about 12:00 PM, Chen Zhaoxiong and others from the Domestic Cement Business Office reported to the patrol station that Xu Qingxiang, who was running the Meichang Construction Factory, had a lot of cement falsely labeled with the "Horse Brand" of the Domestic Cement Business Office. The patrol chief sent him and Western Detective Huaxun No. 309 to investigate. They found that more than ten bags of cement were labeled with the "Horse Brand" trademark. According to the reporter, this kind of cement was not operated by the Domestic Cement Business Office. Not long after, a man named Wu Wenyue arrived. The defendant Xu Qingxiang said that this cement was transported by Wu. Therefore, they immediately detained Wu. Wu Wenyue said that he was an associate of Jia Jisheng, the owner of the first defendant, Shen Tai Brick and Tile Shop, and said that because Japanese "Ship Brand" cement was now prohibited, falsely labeling it with the "Horse Brand" of the Domestic Cement Business Office could avoid inspection. At that time, he and the Western detective brought Wu into the patrol station. Judge Huang severely interrogated the defendant Jia Jisheng, who testified that there was no Wu Wenyue in his shop, and that he knew nothing about the accusations made by the plaintiff. Xu Qingxiang testified that on the 12th of last month, a man named Wu Wenyue transported more than 30 bags of "Horse Brand" cement. His factory was temporarily short of cement, so he accepted it. Later, he learned that it was Japanese goods masquerading as domestic goods and negotiated with Wu to return it. Wu then drove it away. He originally purchased the goods with money. The plaintiff accused him of colluding, which was a false accusation. He requested to be vindicated. Judge Huang then adjourned the hearing and ordered it to be rescheduled to summon Wu Wenyue, the second defendant, who had not yet arrived, and to summon the witness, Western Detective Huaxun No. 309 of the Huishan Patrol Station, to court for further questioning.

The Western Clothing Industry Association

Promotes Domestic Woolen Fabrics

The Shanghai Western Clothing Industry Association, in view of the fact that woolen fabrics are the raw materials needed by the industry, especially imported woolen fabrics which flood the market and cause a great outflow of profits every year, recently heard that the association, based on the resolution of the Fourth Members' Representative Conference, intends to actively promote domestic woolen fabrics to stop the leakage of wealth. They specially sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, saying: "Respected Sirs, Woolen fabrics have a wide range of uses, but they are mostly needed for making clothes, especially coats, uniforms, and Western-style clothes, etc., which are mostly made of woolen fabrics. Our association is aware that imported goods flood the market and cause a great outflow of profits. In addition to informing members at any time to encourage customers to use domestic woolen fabrics as raw materials for making Western clothes, we intend to actively promote domestic woolen fabrics to stop the leakage of wealth. It has been resolved by the Fourth Members' Representative Conference to send samples to the association from various domestic woolen fabric factories so that we can introduce them for adoption, etc., which is recorded in the case file. We have long known that your association leads the merchants and can devote itself to promoting domestic goods. We hereby send a letter to request that you inform various domestic woolen fabric factories in the area of this city to send fine samples, indicating the type and price, to the association so that they can be introduced and promoted, which is indeed a matter of public interest." Sincerely, The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Detention Unsuccessful, Surrenders Himself

After Interrogation, He is Still Detained Awaiting Judgment

He said that he turned to a sailor from Ningbo on a certain ship. He then handed him a handgun and one hundred bullets and taught him how to shoot. So one bullet was missing. The total price was 60 yuan, and he also gave him a reward of 5 yuan. The defendant confessed that he was a sentry at a certain dock. Sun was a foreman of a sand and gravel gang and asked him to buy a handgun for him. He said that he was an office worker and could not buy it for him, so he told him to find a way to buy it himself. Lawyer Fan defended him. Judge Zhao Linyu ordered Hua Zhenpu to be detained and set a date for sentencing.

Gu Weiping's Fraud Exposed

Impersonating a Lawyer's Assistant

Forging Official Government Commissions
