Suffocating a Woman and Performing a Great Coffin Splitting

The Black Dog Mistaken for a Yellow Dog

The case of a woman suffocated in the attic of the second landlord, Lu Hou, a native of Nanjing, at No. 13 Shude Lane, Xujiahui Town, Huxi, has been reported in detail in previous reports. After the local security officer reported the case to the court for an autopsy, it was found that there were no family members. He was ordered to temporarily place her in a temple. Unexpectedly, it was discovered by a group of flower gambling enthusiasts who went to the altar that night to seek dreams. Dozens of people went to the altar, and in the middle of the night, they dreamed of her transformed into a yellow dog. The next day, they all went to the flower gambling listening posts in the nearby Haige Lane and Xiaoyou Lane and publicly bet on the yellow dog as a long shot. Unexpectedly, things went against their wishes, and the character that came out was actually a black dog, leading to their defeat. Everyone became angry at the wronged ghost and, the night before last, used an axe to split open the coffin, stripped off the clothes of the corpse, and abandoned it outside the coffin. The quilt and bedding were all stolen. It was not until noon yesterday that someone discovered it and reported it to the local security officer, who ordered it to be buried on behalf of the family.

The Great China Science Research Society

Visited the Chinese Chemical Industry Society Yesterday

The Great China Science Research Society was established in 1925 as the only organization promoting popular science. It was initially led by Wu Zhihui and successively edited the "Science Weekly" of the Beijing Jingbao and the Shanghai Republic Daily. It was suspended for some reason. This year, it was revived by some members, and the "Science World" was appended to the Chen Bao in this port, which was quite popular with the society. Recently, it has been divided into groups according to the nature of the subjects and is preparing to set up a small-scale "Science Library" and laboratory in Shanghai, and has found more than 200 acres of farmland in the Jinshu of Zhejiang Province, which is planned to be used for agricultural testing. A few days ago, Ling, a member of the society, went to negotiate. Yesterday, more than 40 ordinary members of the society in this port, together with Xu Zhi of the society, visited the Chinese Chemical Industry Society on Binlang Road. Hong and Sun of the factory hosted and accompanied them on a tour of the factory for three hours. Detailed opinions will be published in the next issue of "Science World." The "Winter Supplies," "Tonics," and "Radio" special issues of this publication are especially valuable. The society is widely recruiting members. Anyone who wishes to join is welcome, regardless of qualifications or gender, and can send a letter to the society or the Chen Bao in this port for forwarding.

Xi Zhuting Missing

Xi Shengtin, a native of Jingjiang, sold miscellaneous goods to various cargo transport companies. This time, the goods he transported were sold at a loss due to poor market conditions. Last month, he and a friend jointly sold wheat and medicinal materials to Shanghai. The price fell daily, and Xi refused to sell at a loss. The friend was eager to sell, and a dispute arose. The goods were left until the ninth of this month before they were sold. The amount lost was more than 1,000 yuan. He questioned Xi, who had sold them at a very small loss at the time, causing the quarrel to start again. Unexpectedly, Xi and his friend took a boat back to Pudong the day before yesterday. Suddenly, Xi disappeared at the dock. His friend searched everywhere but could not find him. Fearing an accident, he asked a colleague to report to the authorities for investigation.

Zhu Songpu's Remnant Concubine Appeals the Disinheritance by His Son

When Zhu Songpu, a prominent figure in the financial industry, was alive, he took a woman from Suzhou named You as his concubine, bearing two daughters, Jinlin and Jinrong, who are now both adults. In the ninth year of the Republic (1920), Songpu suddenly suffered a severe illness that was unresponsive to medicine. You, behind everyone's back, cut flesh from her thigh to cure her husband. This act was known to Songpu, who then provided a deposit of five thousand yuan in the name of "Liangxin Ji" (Good Conscience Account) to commend her foolish sincerity. After Songpu passed away from illness, he left behind assets of hundreds of thousands, all managed by his嫡 son, Zhu Bohua. Each month, only twenty-four yuan was given to You as room expenses. In these times of high prices, how could this paltry sum of twenty-four yuan be sufficient for daily use? Reluctantly, they had to use the five thousand yuan from the Liangxin Ji account to raise the two daughters. Over the years, the five thousand yuan has been almost completely depleted. The year before last, when Jinlin married into the Song family, Bohua, after You repeatedly requested, finally provided six thousand yuan in 洋 as dowry expenses. After the January 28th Incident this year (1932), Bohua, using various excuses, stopped paying the monthly twenty-four yuan room expenses, causing hardship for Zhu You and Zhu Jinrong, mother and daughter. They then hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the First Special Court, accusing Zhu Bohua of abandonment under Article 310 of the Criminal Law. During the trial, Zhu Bohua argued that, in addition to the five thousand yuan given to You under the Liangxin Ji account, his late father had also provided twenty thousand yuan in cash. This money was deposited in various commercial firms, which have since gone bankrupt, making it impossible to verify the accounts. Furthermore, he had given six thousand yuan the year before last as severance money. The monthly room expenses were not unpaid by him but rather that she didn't come to get them. He also presented witnesses, Songpu's younger brothers Liansheng and Chunsheng, to testify that they knew for certain that Songpu had given You twenty thousand yuan in addition to the five thousand yuan during his lifetime. You also presented her elder uncle, Xingsheng, to testify that there was no such money. The court then ruled Zhu Bohua not guilty, and the related civil suit was transferred to the civil court for trial. You, dissatisfied with the verdict, hired three lawyers, Zhan Jifeng, Qin Liankui, and Yao Zhaoli, to appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court. Their reasoning included: ㈠ The six thousand yuan for the eldest daughter's marriage in the nineteenth year of the Republic (1930) was clearly for her dowry, as her elder uncle Xingsheng can testify. The defendant presented a document claiming severance and a receipt for six thousand yuan, but the appellant did not sign it, and the handwriting can be authenticated. ㈡ The defendant claimed that the appellant had twenty thousand yuan in addition to the five thousand yuan from the Liangxin Ji account, but the source of this money was never explained. When questioned about where it was deposited, he replied with the names of bankrupt firms for which no records could be found. Moreover, Zhu Xingsheng testified that it would be difficult for the defendant if he did not support the appellant's livelihood, so the claim of twenty thousand yuan is entirely unbelievable. They also cited legal reasons totaling over a thousand words, requesting the revocation of the original verdict and the imposition of the appropriate punishment under Article 310 of the Criminal Law. Yesterday afternoon, the presiding judge of the Second Branch of the High Court's Criminal Division, Yu Hua, along with magistrates Lu and Zhao, opened the court and summoned the defendant Zhu Bohua, who was represented by lawyer Lin Yingqing. Judge Yu adjourned the hearing and ordered another summons.

The Qinghe Magazine Bi-Monthly Publication

Several prominent figures in Shanghai have recently published the Qinghe Magazine, issued bi-monthly. The renowned figure in the literary world, Mr. Chen 　yi, serves as the chief editor. The magazine integrates the old and the new, carefully exploring our country's inherent　 famous artifacts while also incorporating global intellectual trends. It comprehensively covers politics, diplomacy, society, economics, industry, geography, literature, epigraphy, calligraphy, painting, catalogs, and other fields. It includes unpublished manuscripts from Yao Jiheng, Sun Yirang, Qi Junzao, Wen Tingshi, Zheng Shuwèn, etc., as well as annotations on the books collected by the Liu family's Jia Ye Tang library, which are sought after but rarely seen. Since the advent of magazines, there has never been one so rich in content. It is scheduled to be published on the fifteenth of this month. The general distribution point is located at No. 161, Wangping Street, Simalu (Fourth Road), where orders can be placed directly.

The Popularity of German "Lion Strength" Brand Beef and Chicken Essence

In recent years, many new brands of beef and chicken essence have appeared on the market, with a dazzling array of colors and names that are often similar, leading to confusion. In reality, only the "Lion Strength" brand beef and chicken essence, manufactured by the German Marta Pharmaceutical Factory using a cold-pressing method, is truly of German origin and has significant efficacy. "Lion Strength" brand beef and chicken essence has been sold in China for a long time, functioning to enhance essence, replenish blood, stimulate appetite, and strengthen the mind, making it a reliable tonic for regular consumption. However, buyers must pay attention: any product with only the word "Lion" is not the genuine product, and any product with only the word "Strength" is also not the genuine product. Be sure to recognize the three connected characters of "Lion Strength"　 as the truly German-made product. It is sold in major companies and pharmacies in this port.

A Local Prostitute Meets a Gigolo

What face does Xiang Bin have to see Fan Aliuer?

Fan Aliuer, a local Hangzhou prostitute of nineteen years with considerable charm, met Xiang Bin, who resided at No. 21 Jialu Road in Shanghai, during a trip to Hangzhou. Xiang was indeed a gigolo. During his stay in Hangzhou, he met Fan Aliuer. Fan saw Xiang as a handsome young man, and eagerly invited him to stay overnight. Xiang used sweet words to deceive Fan Aliuer, winning her heart. However, Xiang Bin had no money on him. Even the inn expenses were not available, so he lied to Fan, saying that his wallet had been stolen on the train, leaving him penniless. Therefore, all expenses were paid by Fan. Xiang also invited Fan Aliuer to Shanghai, promising to repay her and make new clothes for her. Fan believed him and came to Shanghai with him, temporarily lodging at the Xinxin Hotel on French Avenue. Later, Xiang told Fan Aliuer that he needed to take her old clothes to measure for the new ones. Fan did not suspect anything and gave him several items, including a silk-lined qipao. However, Xiang Bin never returned. Until yesterday afternoon, Fan met Xiang Bin in the county, asking him where the clothes were. Xiang claimed that he had pawned them. Only then did Fan Aliuer realize she had been deceived, and she cried loudly. Zhang Xuezhi from the Twenty-Four Gang arrived and arrested them both, taking them to the Second Precinct of the First District for investigation. The head of the precinct, Xu, interrogated Xiang Bin for deceiving and abducting Fan Aliuer to Shanghai, and for pawning her clothes. The case involves fraudulent acquisition of property and has been handed over to the Public Security Bureau for legal action.

Special Item

Report of Judge Feitham on the Situation of the Shanghai International Settlement Volume IV (22)

32. A third method might suitably be adopted in conjunction with the first or second, in order that officers of the Council who have fulfilled the conditions requisite to qualify for a minimum pension under the existing Rules, and whom the Council considers it desirable to pension according to length of service, may be so treated, without it being necessary to make the officer fit, in other respects, the special conditions proposed to be applicable to officers upon the permanent list.

33. Any amendment of the Pension Rules should contain careful restrictions in its conditions, so as not to encourage officers to retire early in order to qualify for a proportionate pension according to length of service. I think that the payment of such a pension should be limited to the two following classes of cases:

(a) Where an officer has served for a certain definite number of years, and is compelled to retire, without misconduct on his part, or

(b) Where an officer voluntarily retires on account of a substantial change in the conditions of his service which is prejudicial to him.

34. The various provisions of Pension Rules proposed above cannot wholly achieve all that is required. The pension interests of the officers concerned will, indeed, be protected thereby, but security of tenure will be affected only to a limited extent indirectly.

G. The Proposed Municipal Service Committee

35. With reference to the proposed Municipal Service Committee, it must again be stated that the original intention in proposing such a Committee was that it should be a judicial body to deal with questions which may arise between the Council and any officer upon the permanent list under the terms of the proposed new terms of service; but that it might conveniently be entrusted with the same kind of questions affecting certain other grades of officers; for example, a Rule might be made that the question of dismissing for misconduct any officer above a certain grade should be submitted to the decision of the Committee, and a clause might be added to the terms of service accepted by the officer stating that the decision of the Committee upon such question should be regarded as final and binding both upon the Council and the officer concerned.

36. There is, further, the question to which reference is made above of the provision in the Retiring Fund Rules, by virtue of which, in a case where an officer of three or more years’ service is dismissed by the Council or gives notice himself, the Council has a wide discretionary power as to whether he shall receive the whole of his retiring fund benefit or not. I think that an officer’s right to this benefit on retirement should be placed upon a more certain basis. I would suggest that where the Council is not prepared to admit the officer’s claim to this benefit, the officer might refer the question to the decision of the Committee, or to some person deputed by the Committee to investigate the matter. The decision so obtained should be final and binding both on the Council and the officer.

H. A Provision as to Arbitration

37. There is one further point, having a special relation to the position of the foreign officers, to which I think it desirable to make reference, namely, the opinion expressed in that part of this Report which is in effect that a period of transition should occur before the policy of replacing foreign officers in the higher positions by Chinese officers is carried out (Note 11). It is important that, during this period, the Council should still be able to attract and retain an adequate number of well-qualified foreign officers, and the urgent reforms proposed may cause a feeling of uncertainty and insecurity which will sooner or later make it difficult to attract and retain such officers. It has been suggested above that officers of a certain grade or above should be placed upon the permanent list after a suitable period of probation. It is worthy of consideration whether this suggestion should be supplemented by inserting in the terms of service a provision calculated to maintain and increase confidence. What I desire to put forward for consideration is whether it is desirable to insert in the terms of service a clause as to arbitration worded so as to cover any dispute which may arise between the Council and its individual officers. Under the existing Rules, any officer who desires to enforce a claim against the Council which the Council does not admit can only appeal to the Consular Court against the Council, but it is doubtful how long the Consular Courts will continue to exercise their present jurisdiction, and what will be the nature of the tribunal which will eventually rise to take its place. I have made certain suggestions on this subject in an earlier part of this Report (Note 12), but a long time must elapse before this question is finally solved. The present uncertainty of officers as to the future has an unsettling influence, and tends to diminish confidence. I therefore suggest that it would be an appropriate measure to insert in the contract made between the Council and its foreign officers a provision that any dispute arising out of the contract of service should be referred to arbitration.

38. Suggestions have been made above as to the establishment of a Municipal Service Committee, and as to the functions which that Committee should exercise, and, if these suggestions are adopted, the area of dispute which can arise, at all events so far as permanent officers are concerned, will be largely covered. That is to say, any question concerning the exercise by the Council of its power to dismiss a permanent officer for misconduct must be subject to the binding decision of the Committee, and it seems simplest, therefore, to adopt a provision that all disputes that may arise between the Council and any of its foreign officers shall be arbitrated upon by the Municipal Service Committee; but there are two objections which may be urged to the adoption of this method:(1) It might appear to overload the Committee, and (2) The Committee is too large a body to be conveniently summoned for the determination of every kind of dispute. I am, therefore, of opinion that it would be better to adopt a provision that, in all questions which arise between the Council and any of its foreign officers which, according to the rules or bye-laws of the Council, are not to be submitted to the Municipal Service Committee, shall be referred to three arbitrators, one to be appointed by the Council, one to be appointed by the Consul of the officer concerned, and the third to be appointed by the two arbitrators so appointed, and that if they cannot agree upon the appointment of the third arbitrator he shall be appointed by the Municipal Service Committee.

39. The question how the award of an arbitrator against the Council shall be enforced need not, I think, be discussed. What must be assumed is that I am fully persuaded that the Council’s refusal to obey such an award may be regarded as an unlikely contingency, but if it occurs there should be some proper machinery to enforce the award.

(Note 1) Table 8 annexed to Volume II. of this Report shows that the foreign officers in the service of the Council, exclusive of those employed in the Police Force and the Prisons, numbered 851 on June 30, 1930. That Table shows also that the foreign officers employed in the Police Force and the Prisons numbered 1,736 on December 31, 1930, of whom 962 were Indian. As to the details of all foreign officers in all Departments of the Council, see Chap. VIII., Sect. 13, of Part II., and Appendix 6.

(Note 2) See Retiring Fund Rules, Appendix 6 to the “Terms of Service for Foreign Officers,” as adopted by the Council on April 1, 1931.

(Note 3) See Superannuation and Pension Rules, Appendix 5 to the “Terms of Service for Foreign Officers,” as adopted by the Council on April 1, 1931.

(Note 4) There is a special provision in regard to pensions to members of the Police Force, namely, that any member who continues to serve for twenty-five years receives a pension equal to 40 per cent, of his final salary.

(Note 5) See Chap. V., Sect. 20, of Part IV.

(Note 6) See Chap. V., Sect. 27, of Part IV.

(Note 7) As to the general suppposition of Chinese critics that the “Council System” would, after all, continue to be a permanent feature of the future constitution of the International Settlement, and as to the Chinese desire that the “Council System” should be maintained, see Chap. III., Sect. 3, of Part IV., and Chaps. III., Sect. 20, and IV., Sect. 56, of Part V.

(Note 8) See Chap. I. of Part V.

(Note 9) See Appendix 44.

III., Sect. 5, of Part VII.). Employees of the Council are disqualified from becoming voters by reason of their being exempt from paying Municipal Rates.

Appendix 44.

Outline of the conditions desirable to be applied to the tenure of office and the right to pension benefits of officers who have been placed by the Council on the permanent list.

The objects of a Civil Service system are two-(1) to secure tenure of office for the officers and (2) to ensure that they receive certain benefits on retirement. I have attempted in this outline to suggest what points may arise when establishing a Municipal Civil Service system for the International Settlement, and how those points may suitably be met having regard to the special circumstances which have to be taken into account. I wish to say that the various suggestions which I have summarized should be referred to and considered in conjunction with the summary given in the following Appendix of the provisions regarding the security of tenure and pension rights of civil servants contained in the Public Service Act of the Union of South Africa. That Act, though designed to suit the special circumstances of South Africa, was drawn up with reference to similar systems recently established elsewhere, and may be regarded as a modern type of a civil service law enacted in a parliamentary country. This summary may be of assistance in illustrating the ordinary nature of a modern civil service system with a sound statutory basis, and in suggesting certain details for the outline of provisions proposed to be applicable to the International Settlement. (To be continued)

Shanghai Shen Bao Extra Edition

Announcement

Imitating Foreigners

— Buddha

丨The Ninth of the Art of Living in the World丨

The term "imitating foreigners" is quite popular, but no one knows how to write the "foreign" character correctly. Is it the "yang" of silver dollars, or the "yang" of yin and yang? If it's the "yang" character, does it mean femininity expressing masculinity, or does it mean brightness and greatness? If it's the "yang" of ocean, it means full of foreign air, expressing a happy transformation. Both explanations are plausible. However, I have searched through dictionaries and etymological sources, but there is no such entry. It is probably a new term, an oversight by the compilers of etymological dictionaries. However, since it is popular in this bustling trading port, the latter explanation is more likely, hence the use of the "ocean" character.

Imitating foreigners also means putting on airs. The airs must be strong, so people will look up to you. The foreign imitation must be sufficient, so people will envy you. This is why imitating foreigners is a must. Low-ranking officials go to see their superiors, not seeing them today, not seeing them tomorrow, to show how important they are. If they don't do this, they can't display the prestige of important people. Doctors who imitate foreigners would rather stay at home to hold their children and play mahjong. When patients come to ask for them, they refuse to come until six or seven in the afternoon. Clerks in foreign companies and shops don't respond to the first three calls or answer the first four calls (except for car owners and modern girls). If they don't do this, they can't put on the air of being important clerks in a prestigious establishment. Being invited to dinner with someone who imitates foreigners is even more annoying. You send an invitation, and they don't come. You call them, and they don't come. If you specify that the dinner starts at noon, they refuse to arrive until one or two. Assuming they arrive, they leave after eating one or two dishes. If they don't do this, they can't show how busy they are with social engagements. In short, the principle of social engagements is to arrive late and leave early, just like calling on a popular courtesan in a brothel. This is also imitating foreigners. A young man with money earns sixteen silver dollars a month and spends fifteen dollars and ninety cents on himself to imitate foreigners.

There are many examples of imitating foreigners. I will only cite a few. This is originally a bad habit of our Chinese people, completely a kind of empty arrogance, completely a kind of pretense. Foreigners naturally imitate foreigners in their own countries, but they are very punctual and very polite in business. Where they imitate foreigners, they really do imitate foreigners, and where they don't imitate foreigners, they absolutely don't imitate foreigners. It's not like our country, where no matter what the matter, no matter who the person, everyone imitates foreigners, puts on airs to the extreme. It's really annoying.

In this bad environment, why not try to change it, break this bad environment? No. Assuming you invite someone to dinner, and you arrive on time, they will definitely laugh at you. They haven't even eaten the first course yet, so you came so early. If a doctor comes as soon as he is called, they will laugh at him, saying his business must be slow, so he is so eager. Chinese people have the worst mouths. They don't know their own faults and try to improve them. Instead, they completely destroy the good points of others, rushing to join the crowd in doing bad things. Is this why China is China?

Literary Arts

Song of the Oars on the Mandarin Duck Lake

— Mai Qianzhen

Ah Yan was born and lived by the lake, the color of the water always resembling her knitted eyebrows.

A light boat glides into the painting, accompanied by her lover, casting nets to catch silver scales.

Not surprised by the beauty of the lake in Wu, the two characters "Mandarin Duck" are pleasing to the ear.

The Yue maiden rows her oars at the stern, sending guests to wander past the green rushes.

Time passes like flowing water, hard to notice, after picking lotus flowers, now picking water chestnuts.

Songs drift on the oars, mistaken for immortal music on the lake.

Willow shadows curve along the water's edge, often seeing mandarin ducks bathing in the stream.

Mandarin ducks and I are neighbors, facing the green waves of the lake year after year.

Science

Cod Liver Oil

— Xin

Cod liver oil is known to be a nourishing food because it contains vitamins A and D, which aid in development, and easily digestible organic acids (Jecoleic and Theropic acids), so it has long been recognized as a tonic.

Cod liver oil is extracted from the livers of codfish, hence the name. Codfish are mostly found near the coast of Norway. After catching them, the livers are placed in water and boiled. The oil is lighter than water and floats to the surface. It is taken out, filtered to remove impurities, and pure cod liver oil is obtained.

All oils have a special odor, but cod liver oil's odor is the most unpleasant. As a result, odorless milk-white cod liver oil, sweet-tasting malt extract cod liver oil, nourishing egg cod liver oil, and cod liver oil capsules have emerged. Because each has its own advantages, they are sold at very high prices, but it is not difficult to make them yourself.

Cod liver oil sold on the market is often mixed with other oils to get a good price. It can be tested by the following methods: 1) Cod liver oil turns rose-colored with fuming nitric acid. 2) If concentrated sulfuric acid is added, it first turns purple, and then turns brown when shaken.

A. Milk-White Cod Liver Oil

This applies the properties of physics to make a white emulsion by mixing oils with gum and water. When mixed with water, it resembles milk, with no oil droplets floating on the surface and no fishy smell of cod liver oil. Moreover, emulsions are more easily absorbed by the intestines than pure oil, so the effect is greater.

Preparation: Take four parts of cod liver oil and one part of powdered gum arabic, mix them evenly in a mortar, add two parts of water, and grind continuously. After a few minutes, you can obtain a pure white milk-white cod liver oil. The procedure is simple and easy to implement. For large-scale manufacturing, machines are required. The Western name is Homogenizer.

If you need fragrance, you can mix it in as you like.

Principle: Gum swells immediately when it meets water and has viscosity like glue. However, it has no effect on oil, so first mix the gum with the oil, then add water all at once. The gum swells and dissolves into a viscous liquid. At the same time, grind continuously to divide the oil into extremely small droplets, surrounded by water. Because the liquid has viscosity, the oil droplets cannot coalesce, so there is no smell of cod liver oil. If it is not ground evenly, there will be an odor, and if it is left for a long time, it will still separate into two layers of water and oil. Pay attention when making it: 1) The gum must be a dry powder; the oil should not be measured in a container that has not been wiped dry after measuring water; similarly, the water should only be measured after the container for measuring oil has been dried. 2) It is better to add water all at once, so there are no lumps.

3) If the first time fails, the mixture of oil, gum, and water must not be discarded and can be added to a good emulsion and ground to achieve the same effect.

B. Malt Extract Cod Liver Oil

Malt extract is maltose, and its benefits are three:

1) It tastes sweet, and everyone likes to eat it.

2) It contains a yeast that can turn starch into maltose, which is easily absorbed by the human body.

Contains easily digestible substances such as maltose and small amounts of other sugars.

Chinese refined sugar has the same quality as malt extract, but it has no yeast after being baked at high temperature, losing its digestive effect.

The preparation method of malt extract has already been described by Mr. Lu Ziwei in this publication, so I will not repeat it.

Preparation: Mix six grams of gum arabic with twelve grams of glycerol in a mortar, add forty grams of malt extract, mix well, add fifteen grams of cod liver oil, mix well, and then add twenty grams of malt extract and fifteen grams of cod liver oil, grind until fine and even. If you need fragrance, you can add it as you like.

C. Egg Cod Liver Oil

Eggs are one of the tonics, and adding nourishing cod liver oil has a great tonic effect, but eggs are easily spoiled and cannot be preserved for a long time, which is its drawback.

Preparation: Similar to the principle of milk-white cod liver oil, use egg yolk instead of gum. Grind ten grams of egg yolk with one hundred

Page 19

grams of cod liver oil in a mortar to obtain a light yellow emulsion.

To prevent spoilage, you can add a little bit of five percent alcohol or benzoic acid.

D. Cod Liver Oil Pills

Cod liver oil pills have no special effect, only to avoid the odor of cod liver oil.

Preparation: Melt pure gelatine, use a mold to make grape-like shells, add cod liver oil, and seal them to obtain them.

Humor

A Joke About Punctuation

— Yu Cheng

In the countryside, there was an illiterate man who, for some reason, had made a fortune. While he and his wife were enjoying happiness, she suddenly fell ill and died. After losing his wife, he naturally wanted to remarry, and vowed to marry a beautiful woman to enjoy the happiness of love.

This news reached the ears of a local rogue, who came to pay him a special visit. The rogue said, "I have a friend's younger sister who looks like an angel descended from heaven. I would like to be your matchmaker, but how much reward are you prepared to give me?"

The man smiled and said, "Really? Then I'll trouble you. I've decided to give you two hundred silver dollars."

The rogue said, "With me, I guarantee your success, but you must give me the reward first, and then I will be the matchmaker!"

The man hesitated and said, "I can't do that. Maybe let me see the girl first."

The rogue said, "If the girl sees you looking so rustic, she will definitely refuse to marry you at all costs. I can only hide it from her. How can I let you see her? But don't worry, I can write you a guarantee."

The discussion ended there, and the man paid the rogue two hundred dollars. The rogue wrote a guarantee on the spot and handed it to the man for safekeeping.

The guarantee read: "Pockmarks, no hair, pitch black, feet not very good-looking."

The man asked, "What does the guarantee say? Please read it to me!"

The rogue read, "No pockmarks, pitch black hair, feet not very big, good-looking!"

The man listened, very pleased with himself, and waited for happiness to come.

Time passed quickly. The celestial-like bride that the man had been hoping for day and night was finally married into his house. After sending her to the room and removing her veil, the man was shocked. He rushed to the neighboring village to scold the rogue, "You living swindler! What angel descended from heaven? She's simply a monster from the netherworld! What did you write on the guarantee? How did it become a person who is both pockmarked and ugly, with black skin and pig trotter feet?"

As he spoke, he grabbed the rogue, ready to go to court. The villagers also gathered around.

The rogue calmly said, "Everyone, listen to me. If I am unreasonable, I am naturally willing to be punished. Don't go to the court. I clearly wrote it on the guarantee. This is who he is willing to marry. If you don't believe me, have him take out the guarantee to see."

When the man heard this, he took out the guarantee with a hundred times more courage. The rogue relied on the crowd and said, "Everyone, there are literate people here, please see if it is not written clearly on this?"

As he spoke, he read, "Pockmarks, no hair, pitch black, feet not good-looking."

The crowd nodded in agreement. Only then did the man realize that he had been tricked. He had bitterness he couldn't express. He could only sigh and return home to sleep with the bride who was both pockmarked and ugly, with black skin and pig trotter feet. All the dreamlike illusions of happiness were completely shattered at this moment!

Casual Chat

An Atmosphere of Prosperity

— Tian Fang

Yesterday, I received an invitation from my old friend Mr. Wang, along with two tickets, inviting me to see a variety show. The invitation read:

Our company is scheduled to hold rehearsals for three days from × month × day to × day, at ×× Road ×× Company.

Respectfully invite you to view the show. ×× Company

After reading it, I couldn't help but admire. We Chinese people really know how to have fun. Since Liu Adou and Li Houzhu, this hasn't changed. We truly deserve to be called an ancient and civilized country. Natural disasters are not to be feared! Foreign insults are not to be worried about, but entertainment cannot be ignored. The belief that "entertainment doesn't forget saving the country, and not saving the country doesn't forget entertainment" has become a creed that is adhered to by the majority of the people like a constitution. A slogan that can be put into practice is a gratifying phenomenon. I am truly happy for the future of the Republic of China. Some people say that Chinese people are "poor" and "suffering," but this is completely untrue. There are large gatherings to attend and good shows to watch, so where is the shadow of poverty and suffering? Originally, poverty and wealth, suffering and happiness, are only differences in degree, not absolute nouns. Who can draw a line between the two and split them in half? If there is no rice to eat, I will eat porridge. If there is no porridge to eat, I will drink soup. If Jiangsu is taken, there is still Zhejiang. If Zhejiang is taken, there is still Fujian. If we can't live on the ground, we will live in the mountains. If we can't live in the mountains, we will live on airplanes. Except for extinction, there is always room for retreat. I remember the French novelist Jules Verne said the following words, "If there is no car, I will ride a horse. If there is no horse to ride, I will walk on foot. If there are no feet, I will crawl on my hands. If there are no hands, I will roll on my belly." The Chinese people also have this courage to retreat.

Enjoyment is originally a natural desire of human beings, but it must be based on "enduring hardship." We must know that clean streets are created by the full body filthiness of cleaners, but Chinese people are too smart. They only know how to enjoy themselves and are unwilling to endure hardship. The hardships given to them by others, of course, don't count. As a result, one person is happy, and ten thousand people are sad. One day of joy, and three hundred and sixty-four days of frowning. This is truly not worth it!

Writing this far, someone said to me, "Even just one day of joy is better than a year of frowning. Worry can hurt the body, it must be relieved." I said, "I don't pick up a gun and fight, sitting at my desk writing manuscripts, it is already quite relieving. The righteous soldiers fighting in the icy and snowy fields are too narrow-minded and unwilling to relieve their stress." This is probably due to the climate. The weather in the north is cold, and their brains are probably already frozen numb. Otherwise, northerners would definitely love to listen to Peking opera. When I have the chance, I really want to invite famous actors and actresses from all over the country to the northeast to reward the troops, sending a little bit of an "atmosphere of prosperity" to the frontier.

Family Problems

Deceiving Wives

— Feng Zhao

At ten o'clock the night before yesterday, I was sitting at my desk writing a letter when I heard footsteps on the stairs. Mr. Wang from the back building was knocking and shouting, "Ruiying! Ruiying! Open the door!" Then there were two loud bangs! But Mrs. Wang, Ms. Ruiying, in the room seemed to be asleep, without a sound. Mr. Wang kept knocking and shouting, but she just ignored him. After a full five minutes, Mr. Wang's knocking became more urgent! Bang! Bang! He knocked five or six times in a row, and the door came down naturally without waiting for anyone to open it. At this time, I predicted that the couple in the back building would at least put on a half-act of a full-scale fight! Unexpectedly, this Mr. Wang not only wasn't angry but instead patiently smiled and said, "Ruiying! Ruiying! Are you angry? Why don't you open the door!" That Ms. Ruiying said with tears and complaints, "We have only been married for a little more than three months, and you have already spent enough of my money. Now that you know my money is almost gone, your actions are no longer the same. You haven't come home for three days. Where have you been? What have you been doing? Alas! Ask your conscience!" After saying that, she started to sob. That Mr. Wang still smiled and spoke softly, discussing the rights and wrongs. At this time, I couldn't hear their argument clearly, so I continued with my work.

The next morning, Mr. Wang went out again, looking energetic and smiling. He still didn't come back at night. When it was quiet, I heard her sighing and saying, "Alas! I've been deceived by him again." Until midnight, I woke up from my sleep and could still hear her crying and complaining. This is such a sad thing!

Today at noon, she still hadn't gotten up. The landlady, fulfilling her duty, knocked on the door and persuaded her to get up. I heard her say, "He (referring to Mr. Wang) has an affair, living at ×× Road ×× Lane. They often dance and make merry, but he doesn't have any money himself. Usually, the household expenses are all from my private savings, and he often comes to deceive me out of money to spend. Whenever I want to confront them, he always uses gentle words and sweet talk to coax me. Yesterday morning, he took another sum of money from me, saying that he was going to buy things to give as gifts to get things done. He still hasn't come back. Alas, I don't need to say any more. I just admire their men's high level of deception!"

A Corner of Society

Shredded Pork Noodles

— Ya Shi

Ah Yin's mother woke up in the morning, caught a cold, and got a headache. He said that this was either offending the gods or disturbing Tai Sui. She hurriedly went to the fortune-telling hall and invited the blind fortune-teller to come and calculate. The blind man said, "It doesn't matter. This is because the wandering god from the east is passing by this road and is short of travel expenses, so he came to ask for travel expenses. You only need to buy some more long ingots and Yuanbao and burn them facing east in prayer, and you will get better."

Ah Yin's mother listened and ordered Ah Yin to buy four jiaozi's worth of long ingots and two jiaozi's worth of large Yuanbao from the tobacco paper shop and bring them back. At night, she told Ah Yin to take them to the entrance of the alley and burn them facing east in prayer. Ah Yin obediently agreed.

Ah Yin went out the door and went straight to the tobacco paper shop where he had bought them, saying that they were no longer needed and asked him to return them at half the purchase price. The tobacco paper shop, seeing that there was profit to be made, quickly took them back and took out twenty-five copper coins for two jiaozi. Ah Yin took the money and ran to the noodle shop to eat a big bowl of shredded pork noodles and find two pieces of spareribs. He ran back and said to his mother, "Mom, I took them to the entrance of the alley and burned them facing east and prayed. Is your head feeling any better?"

His mother said to him as if she had won a victory, "Good boy, this fortune-teller is really accurate. My head is already half less painful."

When Ah Yin heard these words, he covered his mouth with both hands, laughing so hard that he bent over. He ran outside the door and muttered to himself, "Thank God, if my mother gets this kind of headache every day, it will allow me to eat shredded pork noodles and spareribs every day, haha."

Film Special

Republic of China, Year 21, November 14th, Monday

(No Separate Subsidy)

International News

The Experience of Soviet Films in Japan

— Ling He

The first time the Japanese saw a Soviet film was in 1926. The film was titled "Battleship Potemkin." However, it was not publicly screened, but only test-screened once in Yokohama. Later, "Storm," "The Three Million Dollar Affair," and "Mother" were successively imported. We know that Gorky's original "Mother" could not be screened in Japan. Following this, "Bear's Wedding," "Death Tower," "Princess of the Commune," "Woman's Victory," and "Serf's Wings" were imported. These films were generally banned from screening.

There was a period of interruption in between. Later, there were "Storm Over Asia," "Spring," "The Whole Line," "Earth," "Soviet March to the North," "Struggle for Survival," "He Who Holds the Camera," "Five-Year Plan," and "Comrade of the World."

All of the above films were publicly screened, which certainly aroused strong interest among Japanese audiences. In particular, "Five-Year Plan" enabled the Japanese to have a deep understanding of the Soviet Union.

At this time, there is one thing that we should particularly mention, which is "New Women." This is a Soviet cultural film, a valuable work, but unfortunately, it could not be screened.

Later came the era of sound films. For example, "Life Guidance," directed by Nikolai Ekk, surpassed American films in terms of film theory and film technology. Other sound films include "Quiet Flows the Don," "Alone," "Two Meetings," and "Zadvenka."

Unfortunately, most of them cannot be fully released, and few can see the whole picture. Regarding religious aspects, such as "Death of the Church," "A Section of His Father's Worries," social evils, such as rich peasants poisoning the farm cattle in the "Earth", mass actions, music such as the International, etc., are absolutely forbidden. This may be unfortunate for the Japanese audience.

New Film Introductions

The Future of German Sound Films

— Modern

│Competing to Sell to the Chinese Market│

The film industry in China has always been in the hands of American gilded films. Those seductive, sensual, frivolous, and licentious American films are best able to cater to Chinese tastes. Therefore, for the past fifteen years, the film industry has always been dominated by the United States. However, in recent years, Germany, which is unwilling to be second to anyone, has gradually risen in its struggle and paid attention to the Eastern market, and it is an undeniable fact that it wants to compete with the United States. The Ufa company in the past was a powerful contender.

Today, the entire Ufa company's works have been acquired by Universal Film Company, so its momentum is even stronger, and it is preparing to do a big job in China. Because the German style is fundamentally different from American films, that kind of realistic portrayal, great courage, and flexible camera shots have left an indelible mark in the minds of the Chinese people. Universal Film Company is willing to do it and dares to do it based on this point. The first work has arrived in Shanghai, called "Dragon and Phoenix Dance."

However, the ambition of German film merchants is not "just this." Following this, a German Film Company was created. Their plan is to introduce the entire elite products of the entire German film industry to Shanghai. At the same time, because Shanghai is experiencing the great threat of the "January 28th Incident," the tragic scene of shooting and bombing is floating in the hearts of everyone. This "Battle of Shanghai" gave the people of Shanghai a very special lesson. Therefore, their first sound film to be transported was "Westfront 1918 (The Western Front)", and the pictures depicted were dilapidated and destroyed houses, battlefields bombed by artillery shells, and soldiers who resisted to the end. It is almost a replay of the past "Zhabei Battle" in front of the public, and one has to admire their intelligence. At the same time, they also have sound projectors to compete with American machines.

In summary, the struggle between German and American films has begun. However, the responsibility of our filmmakers in China is relatively heavier from now on. To allow foreigners to come to our China and take over the host's role, like a country losing extraterritorial rights, letting foreign aggression run rampant, until what day will it end?

"The Western Front" is produced by German Film Company and is a war masterpiece aimed at the American film "All Quiet on the Western Front."

Anecdotes of the Film Industry

The Evolution of the Style of Domestic Films and Future Trends

— Ji Zhong

Domestic films, which are very rare, have been around for more than ten years since their inception. Although this period is not long, there have indeed been several changes in its course. Now, I will briefly record it and add a kind of prediction, that is, the future trend.

In the beginning, so-called domestic films were simply a mess, a terrible state of affairs. Of course, there was no art to speak of, and society did not pay much attention to it, regarding it as a street performance. The "Orphan Saves Ancestors" produced by Star Film Company caused a sensation and broke a bloody path for the domestic film industry. Film companies were established one after another. At that time, the style mostly focused on social descriptions, revealing layers of dark secrets as much as possible, so it was called a social film. Tianyi and Great China were engaged in the production of unofficial history films, which indirectly created the rise of costume films. The news spread that it seemed that only costume films were possible, so that was the first period of change, from the social style to the costume style.

Seeing that costume films had become exhausted, China Drama and United Film two companies opened up new avenues and engaged in the creation of martial arts films. The popularity of "White Hibiscus" and "Shandong Heroes" was welcomed. Domestic film circles, who were good at imitating, also changed course to each other, so this was the second period of change, from costume to martial arts.

When prosperity reaches its peak, it must be balanced. The martial arts films that were popular for a while were also eliminated. After the opening of the Star Film Company's mythological film "Burning of the Red Lotus Temple," it achieved unexpected success in business. As a result, domestic films generally believed that it was necessary to "burn." This was the third period of change, from martial arts to mythology.

Due to the vigorous and resolute action of the Capital Film Censorship Committee, mythological films were on the verge of collapse. Coincidentally, imported sound films were popular, and domestic films flocked to the production of sound films. This was the fourth period of change, from mythology to sound.

Domestic films are still going through the sound wave, but recently there have been some signs of decline. Imperceptibly, they will gradually tend towards a road of wild customs, hunting beast films. As for more future changes, no one dares to predict.

Brief History of Star Film Company

A Realistic Sketch of Garbo's Childhood

— Translated by He

The location is Stockholm, the capital of Sweden.

In a small courtyard behind an apartment building, a girl is playing, talking to her dolls, teasing them like children. She walks back and forth, her hands moving, her postures changing, her voice gentle, sometimes cooing, sometimes laughing. She has rich emotions and loves to act, often acting.

This courtyard is no different from any other courtyard in Stockholm. A patch of green grass reveals patches of gray earth. The sunlight scatters its joy and warmth, truly a small, shaded place, especially on cool summer evenings.

But the girl playing with her doll makes that courtyard even more prominent. She is our Greta, Greta Gustafsson.

Time passes pleasantly and peacefully, and the girl gradually grows up. She has discarded her doll and replaced it with schoolbooks. But her love for acting is still the same as before, perhaps even more intense.

This small courtyard is still her playground; still the center of her dreams, ambitions, and hopes. And now it has become a stage, because here she often gathers many children to play acting games. She instructs them on how to move, tells them what to do, always guiding them with a joyful smile and enthusiasm, jumping and running around.

"You be the mother," she orders, "you be the father, you be the little brother..."

Thus, among a group of children and some older people, various games are performed, full of children's fantasies and children's love for acting, but with an intention controlling the whole.

Time passes year after year. One summer evening, the girl sits in an open-air theater near her home, watching actors and actresses perform their roles. She is not only happy but also feels a different kind of interest. Here, her inner personality is revealed.

Several years later, her friends know that she is working as a film actress, but they are not surprised. This was what they expected. They talk about the scene in the small courtyard after dinner or in the evening when they were children, nodding their heads in deep understanding.

Later, Greta's reputation in the film industry suddenly increases. She leaves Stockholm, leaves this small courtyard, parks, and shade, but she constantly brings infinite glory to her hometown. In the dark theaters, people who used to play with her when she was a child watch her perform the drama of life; her childhood friends praise her and say that they are not surprised by Greta's fame.

Her childhood fantasies have come true.

Her brother and I are sitting together in a cafe on the veranda of a famous Stockholm hotel. Across a small stream to our right stands a royal castle. We sit in its quiet shade, looking past many rows of pointed roofs to see the old city where Garbo grew up. The Swedish prince and his friends are sitting in the corner of the cafe, about three tables away from us. (To be continued)

What I See

— Hu Zheming

If every Chinese person stopped watching imported films, I think the amount of money flowing out of China each year could be reduced by at least several million dollars. (But it's more than that.)

If the money spent on watching imported films were donated to the Northeast Volunteer Army, I think at least several thousand more enemies could be killed.

If our dear compatriots could exclusively watch domestically produced films, just like the Japanese exclusively smoke Japanese cigarettes, then all of our country's film production companies could have at least several million dollars in extra income each year. If there were several million dollars more each year to cultivate the fledgling domestic film industry, I think domestic films would eventually compete with imported films for glory.

If our country's film producers could abandon their mutual infighting and work together to compete with imported films, I think domestic films would eventually defeat imported films because our fellow filmgoers will definitely have a sense of national consciousness.

I hope that my dear compatriots who exclusively watch imported films, even if the current domestic films are not worthy of your attention, please still have some national consciousness, watch fewer imported films, and save some vitality for the country. Although art has no borders, it is unbearable to let money flow out of the country for entertainment when the country is facing difficulties.

I hope that the editors of film publications will work hard to promote domestic films, use a fair attitude to criticize and guide, and do not act as volunteer promoters exclusively for imported films. (Gratitude is offered)

Film Essay

The Eyes Are the Windows of the Soul

— Chen Dabe

Among all the organs of the human body, the eyes are the most powerful in expressing emotions. The muscles of the eyes directly penetrate into the middle of the brain, uniting psychological activities with physical activities. These muscles have a spiritual power that other organs do not possess. The eyes, face, and head are the three most important parts of the body for expressing emotions. Without these three parts, we cannot talk about the art of performance. If an actor closes his eyes or completely covers his head, no matter how beautiful the movements of any part of his body, the emotions in his heart cannot be expressed.

For example, in a dance or on a speech stage, when someone suddenly stands in the center of the stage, the eyes of the audience will definitely be fixed on his face, and from his face, they will concentrate on his eyes. What the audience pays the most attention to is this person's eyes.

When two people meet for the first time, you look into my eyes, and I look into your eyes. Will the two people love each other or hate each other in the future? This question is largely decided at the moment when these four eyes meet. The same is true for two fighting animals, such as dogs and cats. Before any power is compared, the first thing the two sides compare is their eyesight. This is the knowledge we get from our daily observations.

Why is that? Because everyone believes that the other person's intentions can be detected from his eyes, because everyone believes that the eyes are the windows of the soul, and the depths of a person's soul can be found inside the pupils.
